I have dedicated this book to you, my sons, for I have completed it for you, this part of the science of medicine, with its clarity and beauty. I saw that it was worthy of being completed for you in this treatise, which is a part of the work with the hand.
Because the work with the hand is noble in our country and in our time, it is abandoned, until it seems that its science is forgotten and its effects are cut off. And there remained of it only a few scattered drawings in the books of the ancients, which the ignoramuses and the charlatans had corrupted, until its meanings were obscured and its benefits disappeared.
I saw that I should revive it and compile this treatise on the path of clarification, explanation, and concision, and that I should bring forth the forms of the surgical instruments and other tools of work, for it is an increase in clarity and a fulfillment of what is needed.
And the reason why there is no skilled craftsman of surgical instruments in our time, is that the manufacture of medical equipment is long and requires its owner to be proficient beforehand in the science of anatomy, which Galen described. Until he understands the functions of the organs, their positions, connections, and disconnections, and knows the bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers, and their exits, as well as the pulsating arteries and their branches.
Therefore, Hippocrates said that many are called physicians by name, but few in deed, and none excel in the craft of surgery. We have mentioned this aspect in the introduction to this book.
Because he who is not knowledgeable in what we mentioned of anatomy will not be safe from falling into mistakes that kill people, as I have seen many who pretend to know this science without knowledge or understanding.
And that is because I saw a foolish doctor who made an incision on the varicose vein in a woman's neck, so he cut some of the neck's sinews, causing the woman's blood to gush out until she died between his hands.
A skilled surgeon had previously operated to remove a large hernia from a man who had been stabbed in the groin, and it was causing difficulty, so he removed it with a piece of the peritoneum. The man died after about three days, and I was called to remove it, so I saw the bone of the hernia and the condition of the affected area that had been inflicted on him.
I saw another surgeon who was performing a similar operation on some of our country's patients in the same way.
A black attendant had a fracture in his leg near the ankle with a wound, so the surgeon quickly applied the reduction to the wound using sutures and bandages, and tightened them severely, without leaving any space for the wound to become inflamed.
Then he bandaged his wounds and left him for a few days, instructing him not to move the splint until the swelling in his leg and foot subsided, and warning him about the danger.
I was called to him, so I quickly removed the splint and he felt relieved and his pains decreased, but the putrid matter had taken hold in the limb and I couldn't remove it.
The putrid matter did not cease to spread in the limb until he died.
I saw another surgeon who applied a poultice to a cancerous ulcer, and it suppurated after a few days until the patient's pain became severe, because if the cancer was pure black bile, then it was not suitable to treat it with iron instruments.
Unless it happens to be in a member that can be completely amputated.
For this reason, my sons, it is necessary for you to learn that surgical operations are divided into two categories: an operation that ensures safety and an operation that involves risk in most cases.
And I have pointed out in every place that comes from this book the operation that involves danger and fear, it is necessary for you to avoid them and refrain from them.
When the ignorant person does not find a way to the neck and the thorax, take it upon yourselves with compression and bandaging, and do not trust in the wrapping and the stiffening.
And use the best method that leads to safety and the praised direction, and avoid the dangerous and difficult complications.
And beware of what you fear that doubt may enter into your religion and your world, for it is a remainder of your ignorance and a diminishment in this life and the afterlife for your salvation.
For Galen has said in some of his instructions, "Do not treat a bad disease badly, lest you be called bad physicians.
And I have divided this chapter into three sections.

The First Section.
The Incision.
And before we mention the operation, it is necessary to mention its benefits and drawbacks, and in which circumstances it is used.
I say that the discussion of the benefits and drawbacks of the incision is a long speech, precise knowledge, and a hidden secret, and many of the wise have spoken about it.
And they disagreed about it, and I have summarized from their words the least, fearing verbosity.
I say that the fracture is benefited by gathering for every bad alignment, whether it be with material or without material, except for two alignments: the Harir alignment which is without material and the Yabs alignment which is without material.
As for the Yabs alignment with material, they have disagreed about it. Some of them said that the fracture is benefited in it, while others disagreed, saying that the fracture does not benefit from it when it is due to heat and inflammation, because the nature of fire is heat and inflammation.
And it is unlikely that one would treat a hot inflammatory disease with a hot inflammatory medicine, and he who disagrees with this says that fire has already been beneficial in treating hot inflammatory diseases that occur in people's bodies. Because when you apply heat to the human body and combine it with the alignment of fire, you affect the human body with cooling.
And I say, based on the experience that has repeatedly shown me that, although it is not proper to form an opinion about this matter unless one has thoroughly experienced and delved deeply into the science of surgery. And I have paused to consider the differences in people's alignments, the conditions of their diseases within themselves, their causes, symptoms, and duration of time.
As for the other alignments, there is no fear of them, nor of the cold and wet diseases, for all physicians have agreed on their benefit from fire in treating them.
And know, my sons, that the secret of treating with fire is to use it with caution and to apply it carefully with the medicine that ignites it, because fire is a precious jewel that does not exceed its effect on the member that needs it, nor harms another connected member except for a slight harm.
And the fire with the igniting medicine may exceed its effect to what is beyond the members, and perhaps it may cause a disease in the member that makes its treatment difficult, and perhaps it kills; but the noble and generous jewel of fire does not do that except when it is misused.
We have tested it through experience over a long period of service and industry, and based on the facts of the matter.
So I have avoided lengthy discussion, and if it were not for the fact that it is not fitting to burden you with a confusing and ambiguous chapter in this book, which would be like a flaming firebrand inserted into the wounds of the patient, or an ineffective treatment which would only increase their suffering through an impractical and unproven method.
And know, my sons, that they have disagreed about the time in which it is suitable to perform the operation, and made the best time for it the spring season.
And I say that the operation is suitable at any time, because the harm that occurs from delaying it outweighs the benefit that is sought through the operation. And it is not proper to delay an operation that is urgently needed, for fear of a greater harm that may occur if it is postponed, which would be more severe than the internal harm that results from delaying it.
And do not be deceived, my sons, by the false hopes of the ignorant and foolish physicians who claim that an operation which cures a disease will not have any relapse afterwards, and thus make it a permanent cure.
And the ignorant people thought that the operation was like a medicine that changes the temperament and removes the noxious humors, which are the cause of the disease.
Rather, the operation surpasses medicine in speed of success, strength of effect, and severity of its dominion.
And it is possible for the disease to relapse at some time or other, depending on the temperament of the patient, and the strength of his constitution, and what he has accumulated in his body from the collection of superfluities, and his neglect of himself in acquiring them through diet and similar causes.
Rather, the disease for which the operation is performed should be a mild one, and in an organ with little superfluity and noxious humors. Like a broken bone about the joint and its dislocation, it is possible that the fracture may not return to its position, and this would be in the lesser joints.
And the common people also say that the last stage of the fracture is that it is a correct saying, not that they go to them because they think that there is no treatment that benefits with medicine or otherwise after the occurrence of the fracture and the pain, contrary to that.
And the meaning of 'the last stage of the fracture' is that when we have tried various treatments for a painful disease and they did not benefit, then we tried the last thing for the fracture, and it was only then that the fracture became set. Not according to the meaning that the common people have gone to, and many of the ignorant physicians.
And I have mentioned that the ancients said that a fracture set with gold is better than one set with iron, and they said that because of the balance of gold and the nobility of its essence, and they said it does not displace the site of the fracture, but that is not according to the rules.
Because I have tried it and found that it does not do that in some cases, without others, and the fracture is better and more excellent than iron, as they said, except that if you heated the mold in the fire with gold, it would not be apparent to you when you heat it to the extent that you want for the melting of the gold.
And because it hastens to cool and if you add to it in the heating, it melts in the fire and its maker will be aware of that in his work, so for that reason, setting a fracture with iron has become more rapid and closer to correctness for us, God willing.
And I have organized this chapter on fractures into sections, which I have arranged from head to foot, so as to make it easy for the student to find what he wants, God willing.
The First Chapter.
A fracture in the head is one thing.
This fracture is caused by the impact of humidity and cold on the brain, which are the reason for headaches and frequent yawning from the head to the area of the eyes and ears, and frequent sleepiness and ache in the teeth and pain in the throat. And with each collection for every disease that is displayed from cold, such as paralysis and numbness and stupor and the like of them from the illnesses.
The treatment of this fracture is to anoint the affected place with a pure, clean medicine for three or four days, according to the strength of the patient and their constitution.
Then treat him by bandaging his head with a compress, then sit behind him, placing your hands on his chest.
Then put the base of your palm on the base of his forehead between his eyes, so that your middle finger is at that point, and press that spot with your index finger.
Then apply the Zoitory cerate, which has this form.
Uncover as much of the bone as the size of a dirham or a carat, then lift your hand and return it to the same spot or another one if you are pleased. Until you see the bone that I mentioned to you, then take some salt and dissolve it in water and mix a cataplasm with it and apply it to the spot and leave it for three days.
Then apply a cataplasm mixed with rose oil and leave it on until the inflammation subsides, then treat it with the ointment of the fourth stage until he recovers, God willing.
And they said that if the wound remains open, it is better and more effective for suppuration.
And some of them mentioned that the skin should be cauterized to the bone, and the cerate should be applied until it adheres to some of the thickness of the bone, then it is scraped off after that what has adhered to the bone, then treated.
It is necessary to exert strong pressure until it has a strong effect on the bone, until it breaks off a piece of bone, whether it be a small fragment or a small flake, and one feels that it has been separated from that position. The head of the wound is left open for a long time.
Then it is treated until it grows, and I did not see these types of bone defects in some people except through the method of scraping and leaving it to its natural closure, as we have seen in other limbs.
And it is not necessary, when the head of the wound was weak by nature and the first type of bone is better with it, and it is used to work on it, God willing.

The Third Chapter.
About the Non-Complicated Fracture.
If a fracture occurs in the skull and is accompanied by pain and the pain extends to the eye, then apply the medicinal treatment suitable for the head and use other treatments mentioned in the section on wounds; if that does not work, then perform surgery on it from two sides. Either by cauterizing with the sharp pointed instrument or by using the iron.
Or if you perform surgery with the sharp pointed instrument, it is by taking a single thread of Thoom, sharpening it and cutting its edges from both sides, then making an incision at the site of pain in the skull with a narrow scalpel until a space forms underneath the skin where the thread can be inserted.
Then insert it underneath the skin until it reaches, then tie it firmly with a tight bandage and leave it for fifteen hours, then loosen it and remove the thread and leave the wound for two or three days, then apply a dressing.
Apply a compress soaked in oil until the site heals, then treat it with ointments until it recovers, God willing. And if you wish, you can do that using some of the cauterizing medications I mentioned in the eighteenth chapter on cauterizing medications.
And if you perform surgery with the iron, it is in this manner: You heat the cautery iron which has this shape:.
And the cautery iron is called the Masmariyah because its head resembles a Masmara, containing some notches and having a small hole in its center.
Then you place it on the site of pain and hold your hand, and you move the iron slightly, slightly, and the amount that is burned from the thickness of the skin is like half of it. And you lift your hand so as not to burn the vein that is below, which would cause bleeding, then you soak a compress in salt water and apply it to the site and leave it for three days. Then apply the cataplasm with rose-water, then bandage it with a compress until it heals, God willing.
And if you need to amputate this limb with the straight knife, which is kept in the case, and avoid cutting the artery in this non-gangrenous limb especially.
Chapter Four.
Gangrenous Limbs.
If you treated the limb with the aforementioned advanced treatment and what we mentioned in the descriptions of the diseases, but the treatment did not benefit, and you saw from the symptoms what does not conform to what we mentioned as the first signs of gangrene, either by swelling or by burning. Then you should insert the straight knife, until it whitens after you have felt with your finger on the spot of the pain, a line along its length of half a finger or thereabouts, and you leave your hand a single time and you make an incision until you cut the artery and reach near the bone.
But you should beware of touching the joint that moves when chewing, lest you injure the nerve or the moving muscle, which would cause paralysis.
And be cautious and vigilant about the bleeding of the artery that you cut, for there is danger in its cutting. And do not trust one who does not know what he is doing and has not been trained by a skilled master, and leaves the work to chance.
And I will mention later the management of bleeding from the artery in its place in the book, God willing. If you see a symptom that does not conform to this method.
And if you find the diseased body affected, operate on it in the middle of the head as we described, and treat the wound until it heals, God willing.
And if you need to use the knife that we mentioned in the chapter on ligating the artery with the straight knife, then it is a better knife than this one and more effective.
The Fifth Section.
Treatment of Hemorrhoids of the Nose.
If a hemorrhoid occurs in the nose and is accompanied by cold and ulceration, and it is treated with ointments and other treatments mentioned in the chapter, but the pain does not subside, then cauterize the aforementioned spot.
Then touch it after warming it around the nose, all of it, as it rotates or revolves around both of them, if the pain is in both of them. And afterwards, with the cauterizing iron, from the root of the nose, a little after marking the spot with ink, and it will be about ten points on each nostril or thereabouts, then treat the spots until he recovers, God willing.
The Sixth Section.
Treatment of Hernia.
The hernia that is treated with cauterization, it is the type that occurs due to phlegm, as I mentioned in the chapter on diseases.
And avoid cauterizing the type that occurs due to fracture and nerve stretching.
When I treated this type of hernia with purges and rubefacients and gargles, it did not respond to my treatment, so it is necessary to strengthen the weakened area with three cauterizations. One at the root of the nose, and the second a little below its base, and the third at the meeting point of the lips.
And make your cauterization on the opposite side of the affected area, because relaxation only occurs on the side that appears healthy.
And the form of the cauterization is that you make a line on the upper side of the nose, below the horn of the head, a little, and another in the base, and its length will be according to the length of the fingers.
Lower the cauterizing iron with your hand until you burn to the extent of half the thickness of the skin, and this is the form of the branding, which is a type of scarring that I have described, except that it is slightly more superficial, as you see. It is desirable to let the suturing thread be slightly thick, then deal with the site as mentioned earlier until it heals, God willing.
The Seventh Chapter.
Treating Chronic Ulcers.
If you have treated the ulcer as we mentioned and the treatment did not benefit it, and it was not in a critical condition, then treat it with four kyats. On every head of the wound, one kyat and another in the middle of the head as we mentioned, and a kyat at the end of the head according to what has been presented.
The application of the makawi is as previously mentioned, and it may also be applied with a kyat on the orifice of the intestine, so it will be more effective, then deal with it according to what has been presented.
The Eighth Chapter.
Treating Abscesses.
That which is caused by phlegm, it is desirable to evacuate the critical condition first from the large arteries and the fine veins of the brain.
Then, he evacuates all of its contents and carries it to the back of the vertebrae, where the thick, congealed blood is stuck in the hollow of the vertebrae, carrying it many times, so that it hits with the kyat.
And do that on the same rank, as mentioned there, for it is emptied by that, and then treat it with three kyats at the back of its head, being a straight line from the top of the head to the bottom of the neck.
And let there be a thick finger's width between each kyat and another, then deal with the kyats as mentioned earlier; if you want to add more and the critical condition is inclined towards that, then treat it with the middle kyat.
If you want to add more, then treat it on the horns and deal with it until it heals, and the makawa will be in a zaituniyya form according to what has been presented.

The Eleventh Operation.
On the Excision of Malignant Ulcers.
If the cause of the malignant ulcer is a putrid and dense abscess, we should open it with the instruments mentioned in the chapter on abscesses.
If the cause of the malignant ulcer is a black humour and the body of the patient is phlegmatic, we should evacuate his blood according to what we have mentioned in the chapter on evacuations.
Then, bind the patient's head firmly, then make a tight bandage in a circular shape, then place it in the middle of his head, and let the patient sit in a bent position, holding himself from each side, then take a single razor of the finest and sharpest type.
Then, shave the area around the ulcer with a moderate shaving, as much as the finger can tolerate if you insert it, then wipe away what is in the middle of his head within the circle, and let it be until it cools down. Do that to the patient every week once, along with other good treatments, until he recovers, God willing.
And if you want to remove many small ulcers without touching the surrounding skin with your hand, but rather be cautious, because this type of ulceration is prone to spreading and affecting the brain.
Then, apply to it a cataplasm of powdered Simum or chicken fat.
The Twelfth Operation.
On the Excision of the Watery Humour in the Eye.
If you are certain of the presence of the watery humour in the eye through the signs mentioned in the chapter on evacuations, then hasten to evacuate the patient's head and remove it from all impurities and cleanse him in the bathhouse at the suitable time.
Then, bind his head firmly and open a vein in the middle of the head, then open two veins on the temples if the watery humour has affected both eyes, or one vein on one side if it has affected only one eye.
I cut with the scalpel all the vessels and sinews that are under the skin, and let the flaps be in the length of the incision, and beware of excessive bleeding.
If you see any of it, cut it at the syringe with a suitable treatment, and be careful not to dissect the sinews, and cut them and beware of bleeding.
And two ligatures are placed in the posterior part beneath the osseous convexities.

Chapter 14.
On treating nose fractures.

Chapter 15.
On relaxing the eye's eyelid.
If the eyelid of the eye is relaxed due to a disease or weakness, then apply one ligature to the eyelid with this Heller's scalpel.
If you dislike, place it above the eyebrows slightly, two fingers in each direction, and separate from the temples, and make the length of each finger along the length of the eyebrow.
And do not overextend your hand with the fingers, but according to what is needed for the third of the wound, and make the shape of the forceps on this manner.
Chapter Sixteen.
On the operation for cataract of the eye.
If you rotate them inward into the hollow of the eye, the operation on them is of two types. Either the operation with the needle or the operation with the sharp medicine, but as for the operation with the needle, you should caution beforehand that he should not leave the cataract if it was one that hurts him until it becomes settled and stable.
If you evacuate it at the time of its growth, it will congeal his eye with a poultice until it is quieted down, and if it has grown and stabilized, then put the head of the cataract in your knife, and then feel the operation on the cataract of the eye with the tip, marking it like the shape of a paper leaf.
And the beginning of the mark is near the cataract, then you put under the eyelid a twisted thread in the white of the egg or in the albumen of the gazelle, and then you shape the forceps according to this form.
Then you shape it on the form that you marked slightly, slightly, in many times, until the surface of the wound is like the shape of a paper leaf, all of which is clear and specific, and the sign of correct operation is that you see the cataract of the eye has become congealed and the hair has risen from the conjunctiva of the eye.
Then withdraw your hand at that time and leave it for three days, then apply a thread with wax until the conjunctiva is settled, then treat it with ointment until it heals, God willing. If something of the hair returns after a while and the eyelid relaxes.
Here is the translation:
Make a picture from the skull's shape, then take from the Sabbun's (Sabboun's) straightening instrument and from the Jeremiah's unobstructed (unimpeded) one, weighing each one dirham or its equivalent. Then, they should all be aligned and made into a single piece, and do that with the help of the pelvis, so it doesn't become disjointed. Then, stretch it over the skull's shape you made into a picture and put it on one or both eyelids, and place under the eye a layer of varnished cotton in the whiteness of the egg and the top of the poultice on your forehead.
And put your index finger over the medication and press it slightly, and you move it whenever you feel the poultice getting stuck to the medication, because it finds it stuck like a pomegranate. As long as it gets stuck, leave the medication and move it with your finger. If the sticking ceases, then remove the medication and wash the eye with water.
And look, if you see the eyelid has risen as it rises when anointed with a pomegranate or with a collyrium, and otherwise, then return to it with the medication on the spot that was not affected by the medication, and do not cease until you complete your task and anoint the eye, then put the cotton on it with sweet oil until the inflammation subsides.
Then, treat it with the salve or something else until it recovers. And it is necessary for you, when working, to be extremely cautious so that nothing from the medication falls into the eye. For if the eyelid relaxes after a few days and something from the hair gets into the eye.
So, return the medication to that spot where the eyelid relaxed, just as you did initially. Then, treat it until it recovers. And this is the picture of the shape of the skull.
And know that people's eyes may differ in smallness and largeness, so according to that, let your anointing be. And do not take the easy way of following those who have experience in this craft.
The Seventeenth Chapter.
On the excision of the pterygium that grows in the corner of the eye.
If you have treated the pterygium with what we mentioned in the chapters on diseases and it has not responded to your treatment, it is likely that it will recur in this form.
You should order your assistant to put his head on a stone and hold it firmly between your hands, without moving or trembling.
Then you should apply a cotton thread soaked in the white of an egg or the juice of the Barzakutona plant to his eyes, and then seal the eyelid with this preparation.
It is better that it be a tube made from the quill of a pen, taken from the end of the instrument which has the pterygium, and if you cannot get that, then it should be from the other end. Even if it were possible to make it from the reed, still this tube would be better for your operation, God willing.
Then you should dissect the pterygium, if it is open and the humor comes out of it, and you should remove its contents. If it were not open, you should open it and extract its contents. Then you should apply the preparation to it, and it will adhere strongly. You should hold it with your hand until you reach the bone.
And withdraw your hand slightly from the pterygium near the eye towards the side of the nose, lest your hand slips or the assistant's hand moves, and the preparation falls onto the conjunctiva of the eye, thus damaging it. If you have reached in the first attempt to the bone, well; otherwise, repeat the application a second time, if you need to do so.
Leave it for three days, then apply a cotton thread with rose water and treat it with the dry powder until he recovers. If forty days have passed and he has not recovered, then apply the strong and bitter medicine until the bone is exposed and adheres to what will be mentioned in its chapter, God willing.
Another method of dissecting the nasal bone, where some surgeons refer to, is to make an incision towards the location of the nasal bone and then place a thin spatula in this incision, which takes the form of this.
And pour into it a dram weight of melted lead, and hold your hand with the spatula, grasping it firmly, so that the liquid does not spread, and you should place on the eye of the patient a cooled cotton pad in the white of the eye or in the water.
For the lead will burn the location of the nasal bone and will penetrate it in a wonderful way, for if the nasal bone is penetrated as we have mentioned by incision and treatment, there is no alternative but to make a hole in the nose and return the nasal bone to its original passage, as it was originally.
The 18th Chapter.
On the incision of the lip.
Many times an incision occurs in the lip, which is called a fissure, and it often occurs in the lips of children. If you treat this incision with what we mentioned in the section, but the treatment does not work, then take a small, thin scalpel of this shape.
Make its edge on the flatness of the scalpel, then place it in a straight line with the incision until the incision reaches the depth of the lip, and treat it with a dressing until it heals, God willing.
The 19th Chapter.
On the incision of the nasal bone in the nose.
If there is a wound in the root of the teeth or in the gums or in the roots of the canines and it becomes infected and ulcerated, and the nasal bone becomes separated from its joint, then treat it, but if the treatment does not work, it is necessary to hold a scalpel according to what fits in the nasal bone.
Then insert it into the nasal passage and hold your hand until you reach the obstructed turbinate bone and its end, and do that one or two times. Then treat it afterwards with the mentioned treatment so that he recovers, God willing.
If the matter is cut off and he recovers, but if not, then it is necessary to examine the place and extract the rotten bone according to what will be in its mouth, God willing.
The twenty-fifth chapter.
Removal of the nasal polyps and the loose teeth.
If you extract the teeth beforehand due to decay and moved the polyps and treated them with medicines but did not succeed, then put the head of the file on your finger, then hold the forceps that comes in this shape after placing the tube on the tooth.
And insert the forceps gently with the file and hold your hand a little until you feel the file touching the root of the tooth, then lift your hand, then return the forceps repeatedly as needed, and the file fills its mouth with salty water.
And leave it for an hour, and then throw it away, so the mobile tooth is fixed, and the loose gum is strengthened, and the rotten decayed part is cleared.
The twenty-sixth chapter.
Removal of the tooth and the gum.
If the gum and tooth were decayed due to cold or had worms and did not respond to treatment with medicines, then remove them in two ways: either removal by silverpoint or removal by fire.
As for removal by silverpoint, it is that you take silverpoint of Boqri, then heat it in an iron spoon or in a crucible, then take a cotton swab and wrap it on the end of the instrument, then dip it into the heated silverpoint and apply it to the aching tooth with the file, and hold it until it cools.
Then, return to the area several times until the power of the cautery reaches the bottom of the wound, and if you wish, you can apply a dressing or a pad in the cold balm and place it on the painful spot, making an elevated compress above it until the cautery reaches the bottom of the painful spot.
And if you cauterize it with fire, it is that you direct the nozzle of copper or iron tube, and there will be some density in its body so that the heat of the fire reaches the mouth of the canal. Then, hold the makuwah that has taken its shape and place it on the same wound, and hold your hand until the makuwah cools down, doing that several times.
For the pain will subside on that very day or the next, and it is necessary afterwards to fill the canal of the wound with good balm, and to hold it for an hour, then to pour it out, and this is the form of the makuwah.
Make it on whichever side you wish, and according to what is possible, and this is the shape of the tube.
The 22nd Chapter.
On cauterizing the hemorrhoids.
If the hemorrhoids are due to phlegmatic and cold humidities and have not been treated with medications and you want to treat them quickly, then use the empty makuwah that has this shape, perforated at both ends.
To make the pus come out during cauterization from one end, place it closed on the same tumor, once and twice, if you need to do so until you reach the depth of the tumor. If the tumor is small, then make the makuwah according to the size of the tumor.
Then, leave it for three days and apply a dressing soaked in balm until what is burnt by the cautery disappears, then treat it with ointments and bandages until it heals, God willing.
The Twenty-Third Section.
On the treatment of wounds in the neck and constricting of the breath.
If the ulcers dominate the trachea and it is not possible to cough, especially if it happens with a cold temperament, it may be necessary to evacuate the mucus or to use gentle medicines, then to cauterize the spot in the hollow of the neck at the base of the larynx in the lowest position.
Be careful not to touch the trachea with the cauterization, and do not burn more than half of the skin; then make another incision at the joint of the neck at the end of its vertebrae, gently, and the cauterization should be in a curved shape according to what is needed.
Then treat it with what has been mentioned until it recovers, God willing.
The Twenty-Fourth Section.
On the treatment of lung disease and cough.
If the cough and lung disease are due to cold ulcers and it is not possible to expel the mucus, and the disease is chronic, then make two incisions above the ribs in the lowest empty positions, and another incision in the middle of the chest between the breasts.
And the cauterization should be in a curved shape according to what is needed, and if you wish, let it be a small puncture with the cauterization that is called "the dot", and its shape has been described in the book on punctures and burning of the ears, and the dots are from thirty or so.
Then treat it with what has been mentioned until it recovers, and a cauterization instrument with three branches can be made according to this shape, and it is hurried with because you can make three incisions at one time, and this is the shape of the cauterization instrument.
The Twenty-Fifth Section.
On the treatment of abscesses.
If the head of the joint becomes dislocated due to a fall or does not settle into place when it is returned, until it becomes a habit for it to dislocate and then dislocates with the slightest movement, as we have observed in those who are accustomed to reducing it. Then the physician leans on his chest or on the sound side, and raises the skin that is inside the joint with the fingers of his left hand if the joint dislocates inward.
Then he applies the cupping glasses that have suction cups on them.
Then he cups the skin until it is drawn to the other side, and its shape becomes four cuppings. It may also be cupped with a cupping glass having three suction cups, in which case the shape of the cupping would be six cuppings, and the suction cups would be on the ridge of the joint.
And this is the picture of the cupping glass with three suction cups.
And one more may be added to this number, making the cuppings eight. Then he applies the cooled cups with salt and bandages, and the physician does not move the limb at all until it becomes strong, and if the dislocation is upwards, it will be easier to do so.
He places above the shoulder a single cupping, good and sufficient, or several cuppings that are beneficial, for the joint becomes relaxed, the swelling disappears, and the physician is relieved.
Chapter Twenty-Six.
On Cupping for Gastrointestinal Disorders.
If a disorder occurs in the stomach, with many putrid and corrupt matters, until they are expelled from their proper place, and the evacuations are directed towards it, and treated with the usual treatments, but do not benefit, it is likely that the physician should lean on his chest and stretch out his legs and hand, then apply three cuppings. A flap under the sternum is made with a semicircular incision, and two flaps are created below the single flap until it takes the shape of a trident, and then they are separated by a ligature, so that when they are brought together, the shape of the trident is formed, and its thickness is like three fingers' breadth.
According to this diagram and to this measure, without excess.
And if you want to make a single large flap in the middle of the belly, according to this diagram.
The incision with which you make this single flap is circular in shape, according to this diagram.
You may make an incision in the belly by making a mark on it according to the measure you want, then make the incision with a pointed instrument, and then treat it with the treatment that is presented until it heals.
Chapter 27.
On the surgical treatment of cold abscesses of the liver.
If an abscess appears on the liver, either due to cold and moistness or to a corrosive bile, until it deviates from its natural position, making a suppurating ulcer, and if you treat the patient with what we mentioned in the section, he will not be cured. It is necessary for the patient to be positioned on his back, and three incisions are made according to this shape and this measure on the liver below the ribs where the arm of the man ends.
And after each incision, a thickness of a finger is maintained, and the incision on the length of the body is straight, and do not incline your hand with the instrument, yes.
And let the amount you remove from the thickness of the skin be half of it, without excess. And the patient should be sitting on his feet, if he is not sitting, then he should be reclining, having stretched out his legs and raised his arms, and this is the picture of the incision.
You may dissect these veins with the Sakkiniyah scalpel, if you have a skilled assistant and precision in your craft, and take care not to damage the surrounding tissue, so that you cut through the skin only, and then cut through the belly and reach the intestines; for the skin there is delicate, so be careful.
Chapter 28.
In the belly and the liver, with a painful swelling.
If you find in the liver a tumor or abscess and want to know if that swelling is in the flesh of the liver or in its membranes, then if it is in the flesh of the liver, it will be found to have a soft and painful border without limit.
And if it is in the membranes of the liver, it will be with a severe and painful border, and you will find that the physicians have abandoned its treatment, so it is necessary to widen the lesion on its sides, then to explore the affected area with the director.
Then heat the scalpel in the fire, and it is the scalpel that resembles a file, and this is its shape. And dissect with it a single vein until you cut through the entire skin and end at the membranes, until you bring out the entire director, then treat it with the treatment of abscesses until it heals.
And this type of scalpel should not be used except by one who has mastered its craft in the manufacture of medicine and has experimented with his hands on these diseases many times, so then he will be able to perform such a task and leave it to the best.
Chapter 29.
On the incision of the spleen.
I mentioned that the masters of surgery have specified the roots of the saporound for the cold spleen incision in this fashion, and it is that you take from the roots of the long, straight, and thin saprouround a single root, as long as you can find, and make its tip like the fingernail, then dip it in oil and heat it in the fire. A single incision in the area between the connection of the trachea and the larynx, and two small ones slightly tilted towards the underneath side of the beard, and two large ones above the breasts, between the third and fourth ribs.
And two more between the fifth and sixth ribs, slightly tilted towards the back, and another in the middle of the chest, and one above the stomach, and three incisions from behind, one between the shoulders, and two beside the outer vertebrae below the navel which is between the palms.
And it is not proper to insert your hand into the incision, but rather it should be on the surface of the skin, making a slight touch. Some of the authorities have mentioned that some people used to use an iron instrument similar to a fillet, and they would insert it between the ribs until it reached the tumor itself.
And the pus comes out, as we mentioned in the case of liver abscess, and in this cavity of the ribs, either the patient dies from the severity of the time or he is exposed to a prolonged illness with no recovery.
Chapter 30.
Surgery for spleen.
If you treated the spleen disease with what we mentioned of treatment in the previous section and it did not respond to your treatment, then surgical incision is necessary, which has three correct approaches, one of which is to make three or four incisions along the length of the spleen.
Similar to the incisions of the liver, which we previously described in shape and size, with a distance between each incision and the next of about the thickness of a finger or slightly more, and the direction of the instrument is as we mentioned in the incision of the liver, and do not insert your hand into the incision, and the patient's abdomen should be exposed on his back.
And the other approach is at the curvature, and the skin that is in front of the spleen is lifted, where the curvature of the patient's left side ends, and the lifting of the skin should be on the width of the abdomen so that the incisions fall along the length of the abdomen.
Then, you insert the suture needles with great care until they pass through the flesh from the other side, then you bring out the threads and make them four, and if you wish to pass by the other thread with the three sutures.
Then, you treat the place of the threads after you leave it for a period of time, until the pus forms, which is a sign that the treatment has succeeded better than what was previously done.
Chapter 31.
On Suturing of Wounds.
The suture is beneficial in suturing a wound that is suitable for it, if you treat the wound with the types of treatment that we mentioned in the previous section, and your treatment does not benefit, it is necessary to pass four threads around the wound and one thread on the umbilicus.
And another thread on the liver and a thread on the spleen, and two behind the ribs, one opposite his chest and another opposite his umbilicus, and the depth of the suture should be close to the thickness of the flesh, then you leave the suture open until pus forms for a long time.
And do not neglect the patient's treatment after the suture, with what is necessary to bring together the two edges of the wound quickly, and the shape of the thread that is used to suture the back is serrated according to its previous shape, and the one that is used to suture the back is zigzagged.
Chapter 32.
On Suturing of Legs and Thighs.
If you find that the wound has become inflamed and yellow pus has collected, it is necessary to suture on the back of the foot at the joint between the ankle and the toes.
And place your hand on the thread and do not twist it, then raise your hand and do not press it down, for it attracts the yellow pus and the suture is on this shape.

The vein that is opened without treatment for a long time becomes inflamed, and the water collects in it, then it is treated with the aforementioned method.
Chapter Thirty-Three.
On the vein of forgetfulness.
If the forgetfulness is due to cold and moist humors, which weaken the retaining and attracting powers in the stomach and intestines, and it was treated with various treatments but did not improve, and I saw that the patient's vein was obstructed and its power was greatly diminished on his stomach. Chapter Thirty-Four.
On the vein of haemorrhoids.
If there were many chronic haemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and it was due to cold, dry, or moist humors, and it was treated with what we mentioned in the chapter, but the treatment did not benefit, then I applied three veins at the bottom of the spine under the buttocks, a little triangle-shaped.
And a vein under the navel like two fingers, and I thought that his stomach was cold and its digestion did not take place, and I saw his face pale, so I applied a large vein on the stomach as mentioned previously, and a vein on his liver. The 35th Section.
On the dissection of the veins.
After cutting them, if you cut the vein, beware of the mouth that resembles a nerve, then insert the cannula into the vein itself and move your hand until you reach the mouth of the artery from which the blood flows, do it once or twice.
If there were many veins, treat each one according to what we have described, then apply the corresponding ointments until it heals; and if the vein was large on the side of the thigh, it would be more effective in the treatment.
The 36th Section.
On the excision of the nasal polyp that is in the nostrils and their surroundings.
If the vein did not retract to the suture and the operation that we described in its place, and you were unable to do that, perhaps it was because of the nasal polyp; so if one of the nasal polyps grew and obstructed the passage, first you should try to remove it with a thin scalpel.
Then feel the size of the polyp with the scalpel, then beware of the cannula that resembles a nerve, and insert it gently into the nasal polyp itself, on the straightness of the polyp's base and the size that the scalpel entered, and apply the vein to it until you remove all those obstructing bodies once or twice or thrice according to your need.
And beware of damaging a nerve if there was one, or a large artery, and if the polyp was attached to the bone of the forehead or to the bone of the temple.
Be cautious of these places all together, and do not do that unless the polyp was in a fleshy place and you were certain it was not harmful, then treat the area until it heals; if the area became inflamed and the matter was cut off from it and remained so for some time, know that it has healed completely.
If the materials do not separate from it, then know that it is either a nerve or a blood vessel in a bad bone or something similar to that which comes to his mind in his situation.
Chapter 37.
On the Wounds of the Abdomen.
If a wound occurs in the abdomen and it is due to a fall or a blow from a hard object, and for that reason the intestines are torn, it is necessary to sew them on the abdominal wall like the aforementioned stitches, and perhaps a third stitch is needed in the same row, so three rows of stitches will be completed, which will be more effective in the healing.
Chapter 38.
On the Wounds of the Nose.
If a wound occurs in the nose, due to weakness and relaxation from a fall or blows, until the urethra is not able to hold the urine, it is necessary to make a stitch at the bottom of the nasal bridge on the nose, where the hair of the nostrils begins, and a stitch on the right side of the nasal bridge and another on its left.
And after the stitches, on each side, according to the size of the thumb, and make a stitch at the bottom of the back, or two stitches if needed, and the suture will be smooth as mentioned before.
Chapter 39.
On the Wounds of the Uterus.
If a wound occurs in the uterus due to a fall or blows, it is likely to be torn away from the ligament and its connections are severed, and it causes pain or becomes inflamed when menstruating, and it is necessary to make three stitches around the cervix, as we mentioned in the wounds of the nose. And a stitch on the perineum below the back, or two stitches, and the suture will be smooth.
Chapter 40.
The treatment of varicose vein.
You should apply compresses that adhere to the varicose vein, so it becomes an obstacle for its return to its original place, and a sign of that is when the leg is bent on the other, if you press some of them together, and you find the spot of the varix in it, it seems that the compress should be placed on the varicose vein itself like a circle.
After you apply the compress around the varicose vein, as it revolves to make the varicose vein itself in the middle of the circle, and the compress that you present its shape in a circular fashion. If you did not prepare this compress, you should use three circular compresses from the large zinc compresses.
You should bandage the varicose vein tightly to the extent of the thickness of the entire skin, then leave it until it heals, God willing.
Chapter 44.
On the varicose vein of the nose.
If a varicose vein occurs and becomes inflamed, and its cause is cold or phlegmatic compresses, and you treated it with the mentioned treatments in the chapter, but the treatment did not succeed, and it was delayed, it seems that the treatment should be facilitated by evacuating the bilious or sanguineous matter, or by using a gentle purging medicine.
Then, you should apply it and direct the varicose vein to two channels, either a varicose vein with caustic medicine or a varicose vein with fire, and the varicose vein with fire has many faces, one of which is that you apply three circular compresses on the varicose vein itself in this manner.
And you make a suitable bandage for it, and it is after what is between each compress and compress, to the extent of the thickness of the finger, and the zinc compress should be applied, and it may be applied as four circular compresses on the head of the varicose vein itself. If you desire, you apply it with the circular bandage that we mentioned in the treatment of varicose veins, as one circle.
The circle surrounds all the veins and perforates the entire skin, this is a sign of apoplexy in the blood vessels if the injury was internal to the veins themselves and did not extend to the thigh and leg.
For if it extends to the thigh and leg, it will form two swellings on the thigh at the spot which indicates the place of the injury, and a swelling above the veins by four fingers towards the lateral side slightly, and the swelling will be sinewy, and the depth of the swelling will be equal to the thickness of the skin only.
And if it indicates that the injury extends to the direction of the toes, it will form where it indicates by a swelling at three or four points or more if needed, and if it indicates the injury below the knee towards the leg, it will form one sinewy swelling there.
And beware of all swellings from reaching the skin to the point where it perforates a nerve or a large artery, lest you cause by that a severe injury or a chronic condition.
I have seen one and two men whose veins were above the swelling and they were afflicted by it in their swellings, until it reached the gout of the foot and it split all of it, and it corrupted the entire leg, then it caused paralysis and death afterwards; for if the injury was on both sides, it would be on this sign with its corresponding signs.

The 42nd Section.
On the wound of the back.
The wound on the back may occur due to many reasons, either from a fall or a blow or a severe bruise and the like, and it happens when a cold and moist substance accumulates, and the wound occurs in this type only.
That which occurs due to the accumulation of a cold substance, after a severe bruise, should be treated by applying a gentle pressing on the affected area with three rows of five or more wounds, according to the severity of the bruise and its strength.
And the wound should be with a circular point, and if it is necessary, three or four wounds with a moderate circular motion, in this form.
The 23rd Section.
On the wound at the beginning of the curvature.
Many times this ailment affects young children, and its sign at the beginning in the child is that he feels short of breath when standing or moving, and you find, on examining his back, a prominence that has risen above the other prominences.
If you see this and want to treat it, then apply a circular motion with a treatment that is in the shape of a circle, like this form. Take the wound on each side of the curvature with gentleness, and if necessary, make three or two rows around the curvature with a circular point, and let the points be close to each other, then treat the area until it heals as we mentioned.
And beware of using the wound on the curvature that is caused by nerve inflammation.
The 44th Section.
On the wounds of gout and joint pains.
If the joint pains were due to cold moistures that accumulated in any member of the body, then if the pain occurred in the feet, it is customary for doctors to call it a specific case of gout.
If you treat the cold abscess caused by a cold humor with the treatment we mentioned in the section on wound cleaning, and the pains do not subside, then the doctor should make an incision around the joint of the two bones, making many small cuts, and the incision should be zigzag-shaped, as illustrated.
And if you need to make an incision on the face of the joint, then do so with a puncture incision, for if the pains ascend to the knees or to other joints, which often happens, then make three or four small cuts on each side with this zigzag-shaped incision.
If you need to make more incisions than this, then do so, but do not deepen your hand with the incision, rather it should be about the thickness of the skin only; if the pains ascend to the loins or to the back, then use what we mentioned from the incisions in its beginning.
If the pains are in the hands only, then make an incision around the wrist joints as you would make a circular motion, if the pains remain in the fingers, then make an incision at each joint and on the back of the hand; if the pains ascend after some days to the elbows or to the shoulders.
Then make incisions on each side, and do not neglect the good management and taking of medicine; for if he follows the best diet and evacuates the phlegm, then he will recover with this incision, God willing.
Chapter 45.
On Incisions for Gout.
If a patient with gout presents with numbness and weakness in the legs, and some of the skin and flesh are paralyzed near the thigh, and this has started recently, it is advisable to order the patient to avoid eating on that day and to use laxatives that will help evacuate the putrid material from his belly.
Then you should make him lie on his back between your hands, and order him to hold himself still until the numbness or weakness appears, then you touch it with your fingers, and you feel with the pulse underneath the gouty swelling on the bone of the hip, a sign resembling half a circle, its edges towards the upper part of the thigh.
The description of this surgical procedure.
When it reaches the white tendon, he should cut the vein and then cut the artery or the nerve to its hollow, then he puts his servant's hand on the spot so that he does not press on the artery. And you have made a separation between the two legs of the patient and placed underneath a pillow and another servant holds onto his leg.
And another one on his chest, holding his hands, then the surgical scalpel is lowered onto the marked spot itself and you hold it upright and steady until it reaches the bone or you make a second incision if it did not reach the bone at first.
And be careful not to press on the artery while you are making an incision, lest you harm it and cause either death or great injury. And know that if you do not reach the bone with your incision, your operation will not be successful. It is necessary for the surgical scalpel to be gentle on the sides of the young and rough on the sides of the old.
Then treat the site of the incision after three days with rose oil until it becomes soft and flexible, then treat it with sweet medications until he recovers. And let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound heals.
And it is necessary to make his diet light during the period of treatment, so that he does not press on the artery when coughing or sneezing. Then, if he wants to stand up after forty days, you should use a strong bandage and keep it for another forty days, and reduce the fatigue and the fullness from food, drink, and severe exertion.

Chapter 46.
On the Anal Fissure.
If a fracture occurs in some of the limbs due to a fall or blow, and pain and swelling occur, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, it is necessary to open with an instrument at the point of the injury, and each limb will be treated according to its size, smallness, and strength.
And if the pain and swelling are severe, and the patient is free from the first operation, or else you will repeat the operation on him, because it is usual for these pains to transfer from one limb to its neighbor, so it is necessary to follow them with the instrument until the patient recovers.

And two on the kneecaps, one on each knee, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the sides of the chest, and a stitch on each joint of his fingers and toes, and one on each ankle and wrist.

And know that the wounded person does not feel the pain of the suture as the healthy person does, because his body has become weak, and it is necessary that the sutures be from the large to the small according to the limbs and joints, as it is mentioned in the characteristics of the wounds.
Then treat the suture with precise dressing and honey, and other treatments until he recovers, God willing.
Chapter 38.
On the suture of a crippled limb, when a limb is crippled and treated with medications and bandages but does not recover, then it is necessary to perform a suture on the same limb according to its worth, whether it is a major or minor bone, and let the suture be gentle and slight in the thickness of the skin.
Then treat it with the proper treatment until he recovers, and sometimes a crippled limb that is exposed to the hand or foot in the lateral aspects of the back near the exit of the nerve that moves that limb may be treated, and the crippling will disappear.
It does not present itself except to one who is skilled in dissecting the members and tracing the pathways of the nerves that move the body.
Chapter 49.
On Ulcers of the Nose.
If the ulcer is chronic and no remedy from the remedies of medicine has been of benefit to it, then cauterize it slightly according to the thickness of the skin until the whiteness disappears and its color changes.
Then treat it with a fine powder of rose-water and orpiment, and the milk of the pregnant woman, and the blood of the hamam, or the blood of the khutami, each one part, and mix them all together and apply it to the ulcer, and bind the place until it heals.
Chapter 50.
On Cancer.
If the cancer is beginning and you want to stop it, apply a circular cautery around it as it is described, and some wise men have mentioned that a blister should be raised in its center, but I did not see that because I think it would become worse, and I have seen that many times.
The correct thing is to cauterize around it in a circle as we mentioned, or with multiple blisters.
Chapter 52.
On Elephantiasis.
If elephantiasis occurs in someone and it has progressed slowly, either due to the weakness of the faculties affecting it, or due to the slowness of the natural heat, if he is an old man with little blood, or due to the length of time, and you want to hasten the healing of the elephantiasis, then apply many small blisters around it, removing them.
Then leave it, for it will hasten the healing; if you want to remove the swelling with the cautery, then apply the circular cautery in this form.
And insert it in the middle of the elephantiasis until the skin is perforated and the blister is formed from what is below, so that the pus may flow out easily, then treat it with what is necessary until it heals.
The Fifty-Second Chapter.
On the Ulcer of the Lip.
The ulcer, it is a putrid sore that forms on the lip, just as fire burns the dry wood. If you see an ulcer in a place where the lip meets the teeth with fire, then apply many small and large dressing pads according to what is suitable for that place where the ulcer is.
Then cauterize it from every direction until all the putrid matter is removed and none of it remains, then leave it for three days and apply the burnt alum powder mixed with oil until all the ugliness and all the putrid matter are cleared.
Then treat it with ointments that promote healthy growth, for if you see after three days that the flesh grows a sound growth without putridity in it, then do not return to the ulcerous places. You have treated the ulcer with sharp medicines.
For it takes the place of fire in quickly providing benefit, and I have mentioned its treatment with sharp medicines in the previous section, so take it from there whenever you need it.
The Fifty-Third Chapter.
On the Ulcer of the Contracted and Non-Contracted Eyelids.
This ulcer often occurs in the soles of the feet, and it is a rough thing that troubles the foot, and the ulcer therein has two aspects: either an ulcer caused by fire or an ulcer caused by sharp water.
As for the ulcer caused by fire, it is that you should apply a heated iron instrument shaped like an eagle's beak to the extent that it surrounds the ulcer from every direction, and its edge is thin, then you lower it gently onto the ulcer and move your hand with the instrument around the ulcer until the instrument reaches the depth of the ulcer.
Here is the translation:

Chapter 54.
On the Suction of the Lip.
If a lip suffers from paralysis due to coldness or rheumatism or something else, it is necessary to cauterize four or five points on the vertebrae of the back, with one point between each vertebra and another at its base. Chapter 55.
On the Suction of the Ulcer that Occurs in the Body.
Ulcers may occur in the body, which are caused by cold, thick, and stagnant matters, so it is necessary that at first appearance, a point should be cauterized on top of each ulcer, with a gentle touch, as if you had touched it with the edge of a nail or with a long cautery instrument or with an adhesive plaster.
And you should cauterize the pustules at their first eruption, in this manner, so that they do not increase and spread out, and their benefit is not wasted on them, unless it is necessary to do so after the pus has been drained through the incision.
Chapter Fifty-Six.
On the Treatment of Haemorrhage Occurring When an Artery is Cut.
It often happens that bleeding occurs from an artery that has been cut when a wound is exposed externally, or when a fracture or a broken bone and the like occur, making it difficult to congeal.
If any of that happens to someone, hasten to place your finger on the mouth of the artery and press it with your middle finger, and hold it firmly until the blood is constricted underneath your finger and does not come out. Then place upon it a few small and large cotton pads, and bind them on it until it becomes very tight.
Then take one, either small or large, according to the wound and the place where the artery was cut, and lower the cotton pad onto the same vein after you have withdrawn your finger suddenly, and hold the cotton pad until the bleeding stops.
If the bleeding recurs when you lift your finger from the mouth of the artery and the cotton pad becomes soaked, take another cotton pad quickly from the prepared ones in the fire, and do not cease doing that one after another until the bleeding stops.
And be cautious not to burn the cotton pad, for there may be a need for another; and know that if blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped at all, unless one of four approaches is taken: either by congealing as we mentioned, or by cauterizing if it has not been ligated. For if it is ligated, its sides will be constricted and the bleeding will stop; or it may be bound with threads, a tight binding; or medicine that stops the blood and congeals it may be applied, with a strong and firm compression.
And whoever tries to stop it with a bandage or by constricting with a rope or applying burning things and the like, it will not be stopped at all except in rare cases; so if someone attempts that and does not find a doctor or medicine, let him hasten to place his middle finger on the mouth of the wound itself as we described.
Here is the translation:

The First Chapter.
On the treatment of the water that gathers in the heads of babies.
This symptom often appears in babies at birth, if the womb presses on the baby's head without mercy, and it may also appear due to a hidden cause that is not recognized.
I have not seen this symptom in anyone except babies, and all those I saw among them quickly died. Therefore, I abandoned working on it, but I did see a baby whose head was full of water, and the head would swell every day. Until the baby could not bear it, his head would swell and the corruption would increase until he died.
And this corruption is either when it gathers between the skin and the bone, or when it gathers beneath the bone on the scalp. The operation for this is that if the corruption was between the skin and the bone, and the tumor was small, it would be necessary to make a single incision in the middle of the head, about a finger's width, and its length would be around two fingers, until the corruption would drain, and this is the picture of the operation.
If the corruption was more and the tumor was larger, then make two intersecting incisions in this shape:
And if the corruption was beneath the bone, and its sign was that the sutures of the head were open on every side, and the water would flow down if you pressed it with your hand inside, but do not hide that from yourself; then it is necessary to make three incisions in the middle of the head, like this shape.
After the incision, the entire abscess is evacuated, then the wounds are tightened with compresses and bandages, and the area is washed from above with soap and oil until the fifth day, then the dressing is changed and the wound is treated with ointments and medicines, without leaving the head constricted or suffocating the patient with insufficient nourishment.
Until the member is strengthened and healed, and another incision from the wound is examined to see where the bone of the tumor appears and the gathering of pus, because it may be in the back of the head, or in its front, or on the right side, or on the left.
You should direct the incision where the tumor appears to you and the pus accumulates, so you cut as much as possible while being cautious not to sever a vein, lest you cause bleeding that would kill the patient due to that hemorrhage, along with the emission of the abscess.
Chapter Two.
Cut the two arteries that are behind the known ear veins, called the temporal arteries.
When a person is afflicted with acute diseases of the eyes or chest, and that did not respond to medicinal treatment, then the treatment is to cut these two arteries.
It is necessary, if you intend to cut them, to shave the patient's head with a razor, then to wipe the area with a rough cloth to make the arteries appear, and to tighten the patient's neck with a good bandage, then to examine where the artery pulsates and its hidden position behind the ears, which is not visible except in some people.
Then, you make an incision on them with a scalpel, and cut them with a curved scissors to the bone, making that at the width of the head; if you wish, you insert the scissors from underneath the artery and cut upwards, and the length of the cut is about two fingers.
If the artery is cut off and the blood flows abundantly, it will flow to the front and pour out excessively. If it does not appear in the senses of the skin, it is necessary to feel from the sides with three fingers' width and then explore with a probe and dissect to the bone, which needs to be explored.
You extract from the blood vessels whatever is on the middle line and sometimes you extract more or less, all of that according to what appears to you from the strength of the pulse and the fullness of its arteries. Then you look at the wound if there remains something on the bone from the spongy tissue, so cut it off.
For a while, he should be treated with warm remedies, then the wound is tightened with a bandage of two pieces of cloth, and it is covered with a poultice until he recovers.
The Third Chapter.
The ligature of the two arteries in the temples.
If a person has a chronic or acute inflammation from before, due to excessive warmth and heat in the muscles of the temples, or severe chronic headache, and it was treated with various medical treatments but did not improve, we have tried in these cases to ligate the arteries from the temples or cauterize them as we described.
The method of work in ligating them is to shave the hair from the temples and intend for the visible artery in the temple, so it becomes clear to you from its pulsation, and little of what is hidden except in some people.
Or when the cold is intense, it becomes hidden from you, so stretch the skin over its place with the tip of your finger, then palpate the spot with a gentle touch or moisten the spot with warm water until the artery appears clearly and distinctly. Then take the ligature that is suitable for it. Then pass it under the skin gently until you reach the artery, then insert a cannula into it and pull it up until you extract it from the skin, and free it from the ligaments that are underneath from every side. If the artery is fine, then wrap it with the edge of the cannula. Then, cut off a part of it to the extent that its edges are separated and contracted, and do not cause any bleeding; for if you did not sever it and did not constrict it, the blood would not flow freely. Then, pour out the blood from six or seven outlets.
If the artery is large, it is necessary to tie it in two places with a strong thread, either from a linen suture or from the tendons of the bow, so that the suppuration does not hasten to the wound before it heals, and bleeding occurs.
Then, cut the excess between the ligatures, doing that at that hour or after another time, and if you wish to fasten it to the bone with a suture of silk, until its edges are conjoined, so that this action is performed by itself or better, as we have said.
However, if the patient has a fever or a bad temperament, because the doctor's skill is necessary to prevent the putrefaction of the tissues, and it is necessary after ligating the arteries to cleanse the area with rose water and to apply the dressing that prevents putrefaction, and after the abscess forms, to treat it with poultices that soften the flesh, and by bandaging until he recovers, God willing.
If bleeding occurs during your operation from the artery, hasten to cut it off, either with a ligature or by compressing the area with a dressing and constricting your hand until the blood is stanched; for if you are not prepared for that, put your finger on it until the blood is stopped.
And compress the area with cold water until the hemorrhage is stopped and constricted as necessary, and it is easier to fasten the vein with this suture of two silk threads after you have cleaned the area with a dressing.
And insert it deeply until it reaches the bone, and constrict the vein in two places, so that its edges are separated; for it does not adhere to this ligature. And this is a picture of the suture.
The sharp scissors resemble the small forceps except that they are less sharp than the scissors, for if they were as sharp as the scissors, the flesh would be cut quickly and bleeding would not stop. But if there is some stiffness in them, it holds the vein firmly.
The flesh is cut quickly, and this action is better than any other action, and it is easier and lighter. Let the distance between the scissors be equal to the stiffness of the finger.
Chapter Four.
Treatment of a continuous flow of bloody tears from the eyes.
If the bloody tears are continuous and their flow is from the veins that are on the surface of the head from the outside, and nothing benefits them from medical treatment with medicines, and you see the face of the patient has become yellow. Then, make three parallel incisions on the forehead, each incision being about two fingers long, one corresponding to the length of the nose in the middle of the forehead, the second slightly away from the movement of the muscle in the temple, and the third on the other side.
And beware of cutting the two arteries in the cheeks, and keep your hand away from the connection of the jaws, and after each incision, make a compression of three fingers together, and have with you a prepared lint or a piece of cloth to stop the bleeding.
Then, insert the sharp pointed instrument whose shape is like this. From the incision that reaches the first suture to the middle incision, and you dissect all the tissue that is between the two incisions with the periosteum that is on the bone. And you direct the sharp side upwards towards the flesh attached to the tissue, and the non-sharp side towards the bone, and you push it until it reaches the middle incision, and with it you cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes without the cutting reaching the outer surface of the tissue.
Then you do the same from the middle incision to the other incision, and after the blood flow has stopped, you compress the places where the bleeding occurred, then you put a dressing on each incision, with a compress that is wrapped in a bandage or a zinc ointment or vinegar ointment.

Chapter Five.
On treating hemorrhages and fluxes to the eyes from the interior of the head.

And it is in the depth of the head, and a sharp pain is felt, and a succession of feverish fits, so I knew from these symptoms that those fluxes and hemorrhages are coming from many deep roots, and the best treatment for them is this treatment, which is to order the patient to lie down on his back, then make an incision in the middle of the forehead. Chapter Six.
Treatment of what falls into the nostrils.
All that falls into the nostrils is of four types: either a mineral stone like iron and glass, or a plant-like substance like gum and lotus, and so on; or a serous fluid like water and vinegar, and their likes.
Or an animal, for when something falls into the nostrils, a fly or its kind, which does not settle in the nostrils, then incline the nostrils towards the sun's heat, and if you saw the fly moving inside, try to expel it by shaking the head or sniffing with the nose. And stop the nostrils when the asperity comes, after you have put around the nostrils a ring of silk or wool, and direct the nostrils upwards; if much comes out with this treatment, and if not, then try to expel it with a soft tube, which is like a pipe.
If you fail to remove it with a gentle and slight traction, try to extract it with a fine forceps. If it does not come out with that, make a tube from a thin wire and insert the end of the tube into the hole of the nostril.
And compress the area around the tube with a soft and greasy material so that it does not become a passage for air except through the tube, then pull strongly and repeatedly until it comes out.
