Chapter Seven.
Treatment of Obstructive Hemorrhoids in the Anus.
Some children may emerge from their mothers' wombs with their anuses not perforated.
And it may also happen to some people that an obstruction occurs in the passage of the anus due to a wound or a strong inflammation that has developed there, and this obstruction may be at the depth of the anus' hole, which is not visible to the eye.
And it may protrude slightly outside the hole and be visible to the eye, but what is inside the anus and not visible to the eye is usually more painful, and what is visible to the eye is often easier to treat by exposing the anus to sunlight. And look at it, if you saw the obstruction clearly, open it with a gentle push, and this is its shape.
Some of the symptoms are slightly limited, some of them are more severe, and some of the abscesses are hidden between the two lobes, so they do not hurt the nose; if the swelling was in the channel of the nose and had become swollen, it would be treated with a gentle press and a strong pull until all the flesh is extracted.
If the swelling was in the depth of the nose, take a gentle scalpel and gently insert it into the nostril a little, then place it in the channel of the nose; if you feel the swelling with what the patient feels from the heaviness of the smell, then cut it out with a strong pull.
And beware of injuring the nasal bone, then make an incision in the nose according to the size of the opening that has been pierced in the Egyptian method; do it whenever you are certain of avoiding the danger of the wound or take out the nasal polyp and put it in water and sprinkle sugar on it.
And use it, if you saw that the nose had become swollen and the polyp was obstructing, it is necessary to remove the polyp and replace it with another one that has been treated with rose water, until the painful swelling subsides, then treat it until it heals.
If a bleeding occurred, stop it with a cold compress or a piece of ice in cold water and apply it to the nose, and use other treatments that stop the mentioned bleeding, as explained in the chapter on stopping bleedings.
Chapter Eight.
On the treatment of ulcers that occur on the eyelids.
These ulcers that occur on the eyelids may be moist and soft, so it is necessary to treat them with a poultice or a gentle press, and to excise them from their roots, then apply sugar dust on the affected area.
If bleeding occurs from them, stop it with a gentle, lukewarm compress, and treat them better after the excision, for many times they recur if something remains of their roots, and if you cauterize with fire, those roots are eliminated and do not return.
The Ninth Section.
On the treatment of cataracts in the pupils of the eyes.
Many things appear in the pupils that resemble cataracts in their intensity and clarity.
And for this reason, it was named cataract, which is the gathering of a thick humor in the upper and lower pupils; and the operation for it is to look, and if the cataract appears obvious on the surface of the pupil, you move it away from every direction, and make it easy to split open with a lateral incision.
Then, you extract it from every side with a gentle touch until it is freed, then you lift it up with the forceps and cut it off. If you are unable to cut it off except after making an incision in the pupil, do not worry about harming the sight, for if the incision was large, you would close it with a suture until it heals.
And if it was small, do not worry about it, for the membrane will constrict it and surround it. If the cataract was inclined towards the inner surface of the pupil, you would turn over the pupil and lift up the cataract with forceps without needing to make an incision or extract it from every side.
For if you made an incision in the pupil, it would not harm anything. Then, wash the eye with salt water after cutting off the cataract, and treat the site with something that soothes until the sight is restored.
The Tenth Section.
On the treatment of pterygium that appears in the pupil of the eye.
Pterygium is a fleshy growth that occurs in the upper layers of the pupil, and it mostly affects young people, weighing down their eyes and causing them to suffer from flashes in their vision, so they are unable to gaze at the sunlight. Because the tears flow quickly to them.
And for this reason, you see them always bowing their heads and sleeping with their eyes half-closed, and their pupils are under the eyelids, moist and inflated, and the pterygium appears obvious to the observer. And when you press on the site with your fingers, you feel the pterygium between them. The method of operation is to place the patient's head in your lap.
Here is the translation:
Make a incision in the middle of that tumor at the site of the prominent nerve, an incision across and not making the incision larger than the one made for the abscess, and also deep enough so as to cut through the entire skin until it reaches the muscle.
In most cases, the muscle appears from the incision like a white fatty piece, so you grasp it with a hook that you have placed between your fingers and extract it outward, moving your hand to the right and left until it is exposed, and beware of increasing the incision lest the prominent nerve be injured by the eye.
If the muscle does not appear to you at first incision, it is necessary to increase the incision slightly with gentleness until the muscle appears, then grasp it as we have mentioned, and then insert a compress in the cavity and water, and place it on the site and bandage it firmly, and some people apply a salt poultice.
And put it in the cavity of the incision to dissolve what remains of that tumor, then treat it until it heals; if there is a suppurating wound at the site, apply the cooling compresses and bandages continuously until it heals.
The 12th Operation.
On the excision of a cataract of the eye.
If a growth appears on the eyelid, an additional layer grows over the natural one underneath, and it becomes thick, then it harms the eye and causes many diseases such as constant tearing, relaxation of the eyelids, whiteness, and opacity until it becomes a cause for blindness.
And the cataract of the eye has four aspects: either it is due to a defect in the visual spirit, or it is due to a strong disease as mentioned earlier in the chapter on spirits, or it may be that the cataract is caused by a blow or a severe impact, or by a fall, which I have mentioned.
Place the patient's head on a stone, then tilt the eyelid with your left hand. If it is tilted and not lifted, insert a thread from the lower eyelid and pass the needle through the thread from above, making it close to the eyebrow itself, and pull the thread upwards over the eyelid.

The Twelfth Section.
On removing the ingrown nail from the eye with a needle.
If it is a hair or two hairs, the work in that is to take a fine needle and insert into it a thread of fine silk, then gather its ends and tie them with a very delicate knot, and let the length of the thread be about a finger.
Then, you fix another fine thread beneath the first one in the tongs and tie its ends if possible, then you place the patient's head on a stone and let it be near the sun so that the work is visible, for it is a delicate task. Then, you insert the needle into the tongs at the base of the excess hair.
And you extract it with the tongs by force until you remove it from above the natural hair, then you pull the thread up to above the tongs and insert into the tongs that hair, if it was one or two or three, no more.
Then, you pull your hand with it until the hair comes out with the tongs in the forceps along with the natural hair. If you pulled the tongs and the hair did not come out with it, you pulled the tongs down to the bottom by the thread that you had fixed in it until the tongs came out of the upper hole.
Then, you return the hair to its place and pull it out, doing that until it is elevated in the upper hole and you see it in the eye. Then, you release the tongs and the thread and take them out, and bandage the eye and leave it for two or three days until the hair settles in its place and the flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then you can add to it a long hair from the natural hair, so that it rises with it. Alternatively, you leave it until it grows longer after a period of time, and then you raise it.
The Thirteenth Chapter.
On the treatment of the laceration that occurs in the upper eyelid.
The laceration that is exposed to this kind of injury is called "arnubiya" and this laceration is either natural or traumatic, and the traumatic one occurs due to a blow, a fall, or something similar.
The method of treatment is to split the blow, separate the edges, and place a piece of cloth between them, which is attached with a bandage until it heals. It is not advisable to use constricting devices in its treatment.
If you do that, the laceration will worsen, but if you use relaxing remedies such as a poultice and a dressing with rose water in which has been added a few threads of cotton, and apply it gently, it will be treated.
And the key to its treatment is to use every trick so that it does not adhere to the original shape it was in, and this method we mentioned is only for repairing the laceration, not for restoring the place to its original condition.
The Fourteenth Chapter.
On the treatment of the lacerations that occur in the lower eyelid.
These lacerations that occur from accidents are truly called "lacerations" and are either natural or traumatic, and the traumatic ones occur due to a blow, a fall, or something similar.
The method of treatment is to take a needle with a thread and insert it into the flesh, then pass it from one edge to the other, until the thread becomes embedded in both sides of the flesh, then you stretch the flesh over the needle and cut it with a thin scalpel.
If the shape of the eyelid does not return to what is desired, then take a instrument and place it on the site of the laceration, and rotate the eyelid with it, and make two incisions in the inner aspect of the eyelid, and the edges of the incisions will be at an angle from the cutting edge that was cut, until they meet, forming an angle. When they gathered together to resemble its shape in this form:
It is the Greek letter Lambda. Then, you dissect the muscle to the extent that the sharp edge of the wound is below where the splint is applied. Then, gather the scattered parts with two sutures, sutured with a soft suture, and treat it with the mentioned medications until he recovers.
If the wound was exposed from a crack or a suture or a stitch, it is necessary to make a simple incision without shaving the hair of the surrounding area, as previously mentioned, and then separate between the lips with a splint as mentioned.
The method of treatment for the wound, whether it is from above or from below, should be carried out according to what is apparent to you from the appearance of the wound, as it may have many differences in form, and the clever craftsman will manage the trick in any way possible.
So that it returns to its natural shape or approaches it, and the same disease guides you on what is suitable for it from the work and the instrument in most cases.
Chapter Fifteen
On the adhesion of the eye splint with the collyrium or with the salve.
This adhesion may appear to many people that the upper splint adheres to the whiteness of the eye, preventing it from easy movement and obstructing its natural functions, so it is necessary to insert a smooth side under the splint.
And raise it upwards or extend it with a thin plate, then cut the adhesion with a gentle touch that is not a severe cut, but rather a slight one, so that you do not irritate the eye when working, and the cutting should be as if you were dissolving that adhesion.
And stop until the splint returns to its natural shape and the adhesion is completely healed, then instill in the eye a milky liquid that is cooled with it or poured into it from the tube of the silver irrigator, then separate between the splint and the eye with a clean cloth.

The Sixteenth Chapter.
On the incision of the nail and the treatment of the nails' humors.
The nail may be of two types, either it is nervy, resembling a thin, rough, solid white skin, or it is not nervy, resembling a hard, white, compact pustule; if the iron touches it or the scalpel cuts it, it becomes separated.
And it is not fixed with a scalpel, and both types, they only start from the larger vein to the point where they become very thin, until the sight is obscured and the light of the eye is blocked, and the purpose of the work in cutting it is that the doctor places his finger on the stone.
Then he opens his eyes and raises the eyelid with his hand, then he takes the nail with a small scalpel, bending it, and extends it upwards, then he takes a needle and inserts a hair from the horse's or cow's tail, and threads it strongly, and bends the tip of the needle slightly, and implants it in the middle of the nail.
And he pierces it with the needle, and ties the nail with the thread, and extends it upwards, and pulls it out by the hair towards the side of the nail that is near the vein, as if you are pulling it out with the hair to its end, then he cuts the remainder at the base of the vein with a small lancet or a small scissors, and leaves the natural humor of the vein.
Perhaps he will be shown to remove the persistent bloody discharge, and has extended the nail with the scalpel alone or with the thread as we have mentioned, then he pulls it out with a smooth lancet at the tip of the nail, this is its form.
And he should avoid touching the lancet to the corneal membrane, lest it causes a perforation and damages the vein; then, after the incision, he applies to the eye something from rose water or from zinc ointment, and leaves it until another day, then treats it with what is suitable until it heals.
If the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert a needle into it or fasten a suture, it is often necessary to treat this type of nail with medicaments as described in the section on surgical operations. And if you want to amputate it, open the eye of the scalpel.
Take a curvedscalpel, slightly blunt at the point, like this shape. Scrape the nail from above with a gentle scrape, and if you see that it becomes loose and separates, and only the scraping remains in your eye from the scalpel of the needle-like instrument or the red scalpel or a polished and sharpened one, and fix your eye until the last day.
Then, return to working on it until all of it goes away. But if you encounter a stubborn resistance in the eye and a painful swelling occurs, leave it and treat the painful swelling until it heals. Then, return to working on it with the scalpel until it heals, and do not neglect to cure the surrounding tissue.
If the surrounding tissue harms the eye, make a ligation on that tissue with a suture and cut off some of it, but do not make a deep incision lest it cause bleeding, then cauterize the bleeding with the red scalpel or the needle-like instrument until it heals.
Chapter Seventeen.
On excision of the pterygium and what grows from the superfluous flesh in the eye.
It may grow in the eyes of some people a red, fleshy tissue that overgrows until it covers the pupil or approaches it or presses on the eyelids, and perhaps the eyelids are turned outward and resemble a cluster of grapes.
The operation for it is to place the scalpel's head on a stone, then open his eyes and grasp that entire red flesh with suitable forceps.
Or hold it with a hook or a small forceps, then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting until you have removed all of it by cutting, and be cautious not to harm the eye during the operation. Your cutting should be either with the curved scalpel we described in the section on nail cutting, or with a small scissors. The thread is cut according to the shape it takes on the wound in this gate.
If you have cut and the bleeding has stopped, then apply a gentle pressure with a clean cloth or a compress of rose water and a little of the cooling medications, and place it on the eye from the outside with a white cloth to prevent the hot swelling.
If there remains some bleeding and the blood overflows and the hot swelling increases, then leave the eye alone and treat it with what calms the swelling, then return to it with the operation until it recovers. And likewise, remove the excess flesh that appears in the eye from this type.
It is necessary for you to avoid treating every weak eye by cauterization or by exposing it to operation with iron, and do not insert your hand in any of these actions until you see that the member is capable of enduring that work.
Chapter Eighteen

The cataract is a blood vessel that grows on the eye, obstructing the sight and weakening the eye over time. It is necessary for you to consider first if the eye in which there is a cataract is strong and does not have another disease besides the cataract.
So, the removal is that you order the assistant to place his head on a stone, then tie those vessels with one ligature or two, according to your skill, and make the ligatures gentle and smooth in this manner.
Or they are two ligatures joined together in one body, like this shape:
Then, you remove with a gentle scissors those vessels with gentleness and wipe away the blood until you see that the eye has cleared of those vessels and the blood has been evacuated. And be cautious not to harm the eye with the edges of the scissors, and let your work be at noon, avoiding the sun.

Chapter Twenty-Eight.
Removing the Eye.
If you remove the eye with its whole socket and no damage occurs in the optic nerve, it is hoped that the patient will be relieved, then you should bandage the hollow of the orbit, and put a dressing in the cavity without any pressure or tightness.
Then you should put on the eye a dressing made of borax, rose water, and lavender oil, and then fasten the eye from above on the compress with many benefits. The benefit of the compress is that it takes away the pain and inflammation, and each piece of it should be divided into four parts, making many of them.
Then you should put one on top of another according to the need of the eye, then fasten them with a strong compress, and repeat the dressing with the ointment without pressure, then remove the dressing and leave the eye bandaged for a day and a night.
If the conjunctiva has relaxed during that, it is hoped that it will be well-fastened. Then remove the compress after a day and a night, as we said. If you see that the eye has returned to its normal state, then repeat the compress, dressing, fastening, and bandaging until it recovers.
The Section on Hernias and Ruptures.
On the Excision of the Tonsils.
If a hernia appears in the tonsil area and it swells and protrudes outside the jawbone, resembling a tonsil, and it disturbs the human appearance, I have decided to excise it, and I will describe the operation for it.
And it is that you insert a needle at the base of the tonsil from below upwards, then you insert another needle with a thread like a loop from the side of the jaw and pull it through, leaving the first needle in its place.
Then you cut the place of the looped thread and tie some of the tonsil around the needle, and pull it strongly, then you remove the needle and apply a compress with egg white and sugar on the eye, and leave it until the threads come out with the tonsil, then you treat the eye with what soothes it.
Until the wound heals, and you fasten the tonsil from every side with a circle of sutures until the eye is well, then you apply a gentle compress that reaches to the edge of the eye, so the egg white discharge flows out and the eye subsides, and you bandage it on the cheek, and fasten it until it heals.
The Second Section on Ruptures.
On the Treatment of Varices.
This disease, which is called a varix, is a vein that accumulates in the eye, resembling a descending water, but it is not so; and the method of operation for this is to sit on a chair, upright, then take its head with your hands from both sides.
And you shake it until you see the vein descending to the bottom of your eye, then you steady yourself and do not move, and the light is released and the patient sees things as he used to, and if it does not descend to the bottom, we know that it is water, for it did not flow down with what we mentioned.
Then, sit the patient between your hands, and take a thin scalpel, and make a small incision above the corneal membrane at the point where the conjunctiva connects to the corneal membrane in the corner of the eye, until the material comes out.
Then, if only a small amount of humor comes out of the eye, either a humor that has been mixed with vitellus or one that has been thickened with albumen and vitellus, then treat it with gentle treatment until it recovers.

Chapter 24.
On the treatment of abscesses in the nostrils.
There can be various abscesses in the nostrils, including one that resembles a scorpion's tail with many legs, and among them are carcinomatous ones that penetrate to the bone and others that are not carcinomatous but do not penetrate to the bone.
If one of these abscesses is not carcinomatous and not painful, it should be treated by sitting in the sun with your hands opposite it, and opening its orifice and inserting a scalpel into those abscesses, then extracting them to the outside, and cutting what is adhering from it with a fine, sharp, one-edged instrument.
Until you learn that the entire abscess has gone, but if some of it remains and you cannot cut it out completely, then scrape it with a fine instrument, being careful not to leave any of it behind, lest you be overcome by bleeding or inflammation or severe pain.
Then deal with it as is necessary, or if it was one of the malignant tumors, then hasten to remove it until the bleeding stops and all the abscesses disappear, then insert a tube into the nostril after the incision, whether an irrigator or a syringe, so that you open up the nostrils and drain out the pus to the throat.
But if you find that it has not healed, and the pus is not draining as it should, then know that there is a hidden abscess in the upper part of the bone that the instrument did not reach with the incision, so then it is necessary to take a thread from a probe that has some thickness.
He forms in it many knots and makes between each knot a finger or less, and he leaves the end of the thread at the tip of his nose with a subtle touch or what is possible for him after he has formed it like a ring and pulls it gently until he reaches the bone.
And he brings out the loop and often does like this action, which is a simple thing in the books, and it is an easy matter for whoever wants it. Then he gathers the two ends of the thread, one that came out of the mouth and the other that remained in the nose.
Then he uses to spread the flesh with the knots that are in the thread, doing that until he learns that the flesh has been cut by the knot of the thread. Then he brings out the thread and presses on the nose after wiping away the blood, and he does that for three days or more.
Until he eats away all that remains of the flesh, then he presses finally on the nose, a tube of silver or ivory, until he recovers. If he needs treatment, he should use it.

Chapter Twenty-Five.
On the nasal polyps at the end of the nose.
Many times, a growth forms at the end of the nose, a bone-like thing that increases with the days until it obstructs the vision.
And therefore, it is necessary to remove it at its first appearance and to extract its entirety, then to apply to the site either cauterization or the dissolving medicine that takes the place of cauterization. If you neglect to remove it until it becomes hard, then look, for it was a hard, solid, blackish thing with little sensation.
If you do not excise it with the iron, it will be a malignant tumor and I have seen many cases of this type of tumor that have caused great suffering to their owners, and although the tumor is soft and fleshy, I have found that excision can be done in its entirety. You should hasten to remove the limb and cut it off without hesitation or delay, and treat the stump with what will dry it and constrict it until it heals.
Chapter Twenty-Six.
On the surgical treatment of the nose, lip, and ears. If you separate the connections from a wound or something similar, know that when separation of connections occurs in one of these joints, it reduces what can be done to work on it, except in some people.
When you find that something like this has been shown, look and see if the wound is fresh with its blood; then bring the edges of the wound together with sutures and treat it until it heals. And if the separation of connections has separated them and each part is in its correct position, it is necessary to sew up each part with a visible suture on the surface until it is concealed.

Chapter Twenty-Seven.
On the extraction of knots that form on the sutures.
Many people have small, hard tumors inside their lips that resemble a grain of barley, some of which are smaller and others larger; it is necessary to split the lip and dissect each node, and to ligate them with a thread.
And cut them from every direction, then pack the area after cutting with a pledget of lint until the bleeding stops, and apply compresses and treat the areas with what is needed to prevent the wounds from becoming infected.
Chapter 28.
On excising redundant flesh in the gums.
Many times, redundant flesh grows on the gums, which is called "ulcers" by Abulcasis; it is necessary to ligate it with a thread or to grasp it with a forceps and to cut it at its base, then to leave the area for a time until the discharge or blood stops, and then to apply a pledget of lint to the area.
Or one of the constricting medications that dry out the flesh, for if you return to treating that flesh after it has grown back, it often returns again, and that is why it does not come back after cauterization.
Chapter 29.
On extracting teeth with iron instruments.
It may happen that rough, tartar-like deposits gather on the surfaces of teeth, from the inside and outside, between the gums, which can turn black, yellow, or green, until they cause corruption to the gums and spoil the teeth, for that reason.
It is necessary to scrape the tartar with your fingers and a stone, and to extract the tooth that appears to you to have deposits and stains resembling clay, until nothing of it remains, and likewise you should do with black, green, yellow, and other (deposits) until it becomes clean.
For if the deposits that were on it from the first extraction remain, then you should repeat the extraction on another day and a third, until you reach your goal in what you want. And know that the tooth requires different instruments of various shapes according to what is needed for the work.
For the vein that is stripped from the inside, unlike the one that is stripped from the outside, and the one that is stripped between the branches, in another way, and these are several types of stripping that you will encounter.
Chapter Thirty.
The Extraction of Teeth.
You should treat the vein with all skill and caution, and avoid breaking it, for if you break it, it will not be behind, since it is a noble and precious thing, until it does not become bad unless its breaking is necessary.
You should be cautious if the patient insists on extracting it, to reassure him until he feels comfortable about the painful vein. Many times the patient is deceived and thinks that the painful vein is the correct one to be extracted, then the pain does not go away until the diseased vein is extracted; we have seen that happen many times with the actions of the surgeons.
If the painful vein is sound in itself, then it is necessary to make an incision around the tooth with a small amount of strength until you free the gum from every side, and then move it with your fingers or the fine forceps, little by little, until you expose it.
Then you grasp it at that point, firmly holding the large forceps, and the patient's head is between your thighs, having been secured so as not to move, then you pull the vein in a straight line, lest you break it; if it does not come out, take one of those instruments and insert it underneath from every side with gentleness and movement, as you did previously.
And if the vein is curved or twisted, it is necessary to fill that hole with a compress and tighten it tightly with a thin, smooth-edged instrument, lest it slips away when you grasp it with the forceps, and it is necessary to make an incision around the gum from every side, nicely.
Preserve your effort to avoid breaking it, and leave some of it to return to the weak spot, for it is greater than the first encounter. And beware that you do not create what the wound creators do in their profession, and be cautious in their use, lest they employ what we have described.
They often happen to people with great harm, which is that the vein is cut and its roots are completely or partially severed. And if the bone of the jaw is fractured, as we have seen many times, and then becomes fixed with a dressing or with vinegar and salt, if bleeding occurs from that place, it often happens, so apply something from the bandage and attach it to the spot.
And if the bandage does not benefit you, make for yourself a gentle, smooth, and short splint with a soft grip, so that it does not hurt when you apply it to the vein. And this is the picture of the major splints.
It should be as you see, soft in its grip, so that when you apply it, it does not hurt itself or become short in its extremities. And let it be made of Indian iron or of forged steel, with smooth extremities and at its end a hook that enters into another, so that it grips firmly and tightly.
And the extremities should be made like the file's teeth, so that they are also strong in their grip.

In the extraction of roots of teeth and in pulling out fractured jawbones.

The 32nd Chapter.
On the treatment of fresh and recent wounds.
Wounds, if they are not on their natural site, are deformed by that, and it is even more so if it occurs in women and children, for it is necessary to consider, since a wound may be situated behind another wound.
And it is not possible to treat it, nor can its border be seen, and if it adjoins another wound, it should be treated with this method which has been described.
It resembles a small scissors and is made of sharp Indian steel, its edge being very sharp, and it should be used to cut on many days for the purpose of scraping the wound, and it will not tremble or hesitate with other wounds; and if it is necessary to treat a wound that has become putrid, it is broadened by a file from India, and this is its shape.
It is entirely made of Indian steel, and its edge is very sharp, being like the file with which the needles are made; it is used to treat the wound little by little on many days, gradually, so that the wound does not tremble, then it is cleansed thoroughly and dressed with some of the medicaments.
And if a wound has become bent and some of it has become crooked, it hurts the tongue when speaking, so it is necessary to treat it also until the curvature of that bend is corrected and it becomes straight, and it does not hurt the tongue and does not disturb speech.
The 33rd Chapter.
On the stitching of movable wounds with silver or golden threads.
If the wound is of a tender nature, it trembles and moves away from the blow or fall, and the doctor cannot apply pressure on something that can be eaten, so that it may not suppurate, and it should be treated with astringent medicines, for it will not benefit from treatment.
The trick in it is to use a thread of gold or silver, and gold is better because silver becomes tarnished and decays after a few days, while gold remains as it is forever, without being affected by that, and the thread should be moderate in the wound and tightened according to what fits between the edges.
The method of stitching is to take the thread and pass it between the sound edges, then sew with the ends of the thread between the moving edges, one or more, until you reach the sound edge on the other side.
Then you return the stitching to the side from which you started, and tighten your hand with gentleness and precision until the wound does not open, and your tightening of the thread is at the roots of the edges so that it does not come loose. Then you cut the excess ends of the thread with scissors, and gather them together, and tie them with a knot, and hide them between the sound edge and the moving edge.
So that the tongue does not get in, then you leave it like this, bound as it is, for if it comes loose or gets cut, you can tighten it with another thread, and so it remains like this for a long time. And this is the picture of the edges and the form of the stitching on two sound edges and two moving edges, as you see.
And sometimes one or two edges, after they have fallen into their place, are stitched as we described and remain. And it is the skilled craftsman who does that, perhaps he will carve a piece of bone from the bones of an animal, making it in the form of the edge, and placing it in the position from which the edge went. And he tightens as we said, and it remains, and he enjoys that.
Chapter 34.
On cutting the ligament that appears under the tongue, which hinders speech.
This ligament that appears under the tongue may be either a natural one, born with the human being, or an acquired one resulting from a wound that has healed.
Operate by making an incision in the upper arm and dissecting down to the bone, then cut through the neural cord transversely until the tongue is freed from its constraint. If there is some stiffness or complexity and that is due to the plication of a wound, apply a compress and incise transversely until the neural cord is cut and the knot is released.
Beware that the incision is not in the depth of the flesh, lest you cut a blood vessel there and bleeding occurs. Then, apply compression with rose water or vinegar and cold water, then put under the tongue a piece of cloth soaked in rose water, which is to be held by the upper arm every night.
If the bleeding recurs, apply a zinc oxide paste to the site, and if the blood overflows, stop it with a cotton pad and tighten the site with a compressive bandage. Then, treat him with gentle treatment until he recovers.
Chapter 35.
On extracting the tonsils that have developed under the tongue.
It may happen that under the tongue a swelling occurs, similar to small tonsils, which prevents the tongue from performing its natural function, and perhaps it becomes so large that it fills the mouth. The operation involves making an incision in the upper arm at the level of the swollen area and examining it.
If you find it to be a black, hard, and unyielding swelling that the upper arm does not sense, do not touch it, for it is a malignant tumor. If it inclines towards whiteness and has moisture in it, apply a compress and incise it with a delicate scalpel, and free it from all sides.
If blood overflows during the operation, apply a zinc oxide paste to stop the bleeding, then return to the operation until you complete it successfully, and finally, apply compression with vinegar and salt.
Then, we should choose the treatment that is most suitable for it until he recovers.

The Forty Sections.
It is used to extract fragments of speech from the cavities of the wounds and to split them.
Wounds have many types, varied and classified according to what will be mentioned one by one in this book, and they differ in their cavities and splitting from two aspects: one of them is the type of wound itself and what it contains of ruptures.
And the second type is according to the locations in which they occur on the body, because a wound that occurs on the head is not like a wound that occurs on the belly, and a wound that occurs on a fleshy part is not like a wound that occurs on a joint, each one of them has a rule for the operation.
And among the wounds, there are those that should not be split until after the pus has matured in them and its quantity is complete, and among them are those that should be split while they are still fresh and have not yet reached their limit, like the wounds that are close to the joints.
Because if a wound occurs near a joint and its matter reaches it, it may affect the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing lameness in that limb or being close to a principal organ.
For if you delay splitting it until it matures, you may harm the principal organ or it may be near the belly, so you should split it while it is still fresh and not fully mature, which is near the belly, lest the pus flows into the belly and becomes a deadly abscess.
It is necessary to wait until the time when the tumor has matured on the skin, and it is at rest, and the humor has receded, and the inflammation has subsided, and the throbbing has ceased, and the head of the tumor has settled, and other signs have appeared.
It is necessary to make the incision at the lowest part of the tumor, if possible, so that it will be easier to dissect to the bottom or to a more superficial part of the tumor, and not to let the incision be deep in length, especially when the tumors are on the hands and feet.
And it is necessary to take into account the muscles, tendons, nerves, and blood vessels, and altogether in all flat places that do not have a curvature, and as for those that are curved, it is necessary to make the incision according to that place, and if the tumor is in fleshy areas, it is better to leave the incision untilled.
Until the tumor has matured as we mentioned earlier, it is not wise to make an incision before that, for it would be a futile and difficult task, and might lead to severe damage and putrefaction, and sometimes the edges of the wound would not unite. And some tumors may necessitate an incision on the surface of the body at the time of necessity or according to what the affected limb requires.
It is necessary to use a single incision for small tumors, and for large tumors, a wide incision or multiple superficial ones according to the size of the tumor. And there may be some tumors that require scraping the skin and cutting if it has become like a crust.
And it is necessary to be careful in what has died, as it appears in many ulcers and apostemata, and among them are those that have a triangular incision, and among them are those that are cut in the shape of a paper leaf, like the Arab's cyst.
And among them are those that use the circular incision, the crescent-shaped incision, and similar ones among the incisions. And what does not have a head, such as the flat, smooth tumors, it is necessary to make a simple incision only. And if the tumor is large and has collected much matter, and its incision is deep, it is necessary not to hasten, so that all the pus comes out at that time.
I extracted some of it, then I pressed the abscess firmly until another day, then I extracted some of the pus as well. I did that repeatedly on a gradual basis until I extracted all of it.
And beware, for if the patient is weak, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an elderly person, then the vital spirit often collapses with the sudden evacuation of pus, so the patient may die and you will not perceive it. Be cautious of this chapter, beware greatly.
And after you have evacuated the pus, it is necessary to massage the wound and examine it. If the abscess was small or the incision was single and simple, then use a dressing of cotton or soft bandage. And if the abscess was large and there were many sutures.
It is necessary to insert a dressing into each suture until some of them reach others. And if the abscess had cut through the skin or had turned inward, it is necessary to bandage it with soft bandages or gentle cotton without moisture and tighten it until the third day.
Then remove the dressing and treat it with what is necessary from the medicines until he recovers. If a bleeding appeared during your operation, use cold water and vinegar after you have sprinkled a piece of cotton in them and apply it to the place of the bleeding repeatedly.
If the bleeding persisted, it is necessary to use the treatment and remedies that we described in many places of this book of ours and from the section. If you were in winter time and the place of the abscess was very sensitive, it is necessary to apply a warm poultice with rose water and hot oil.
And apply it to the place. And if you were in summer and the places were humid, it is necessary to apply a cold poultice with water and oil or rose water and oil, all of that being cool, until on the third day as we mentioned earlier, it is necessary to evacuate the abscess and massage it.
It is used in the treatment of what ails him until he recovers, and this is what is needed from knowledge of treating tumors on the body and how to dissect them; I have mentioned each tumor and the way to treat it, making it clear.

Chapter 44.
Incision on the tumor that appears on the throat from outside, and it is called the pharyngeal abscess.
This tumor, which is called a pharyngeal abscess, is a large swelling on the surface of the body, and it is common in women, and it has two types.
It is of two types: either natural or symptomatic. As for the natural one, there is no remedy for it, and as for the symptomatic one, it has two forms: one resembles a suppurating abscess, and the other resembles a tumor that occurs from the thickening of the artery, and its incision is dangerous. It is not advisable to touch it with a sharp instrument unless it was small, for if you had touched it and pressed on it with the director, I would have found it to resemble a suppurating abscess, and it would not be related to any of the arteries, so I would incise it as one would incise an abscess. Extract it from the cyst if it is in a cyst, and if not, then drain everything and treat the area with suitable treatment.
Chapter 45.
On wounds of various kinds.
Wounds have many kinds, and I mentioned all their kinds in the classification. It is necessary to distinguish here between a wound and an abscess, as it is confusing. So, I say that an abscess has heat, redness, and painful throbbing until it points to the weakness of the body. The abscess is complete when it causes redness and hardness, whereas a wound does not have heat, nor redness, nor throbbing pain, and it has a cyst-like capsule which is its own special covering, and it is on the surface of the body, and its beginning is like an inflammation, and it becomes like a tumor, bigger or smaller.
It is of two types, either serous or containing humidity, and the types of humidity are many, as I mentioned in the classification. It is necessary that if you proceed to treat a wound, you should clean it first with the instrument called a probe, according to its shape, which will be explained in the following chapter.
Feel the bone of the tumor, then insert the probe and look at what comes out after it. If a serous fluid comes out, or any color that was in it, drain it with a simple drainage as I mentioned in other tumors. And if no fluid comes out after inserting the probe, know that it is serous.
Drain it with a drainage like this, as I taught you, and fasten it with bandages and release the skin from every side gently and take care of the cyst if you are able to extract it correctly with the wound.

If the ulcer is large, then cut its lips and treat it with what will bring it together.

Chapter 49.

The 52nd Chapter.
On the treatment of wounds of the nose.

It does not recede if you press on it with your hand, nor does it increase or decrease; if it is due to blood, then it will appear as a tumor with these signs, turning black; but if it is due to a swollen abscess, the tumor will be hard and solid, and it will settle at a single level.

The Sixty-Second Section.
On extracting the arrowhead.
We have mentioned in the section on wounds the types of arrowheads and their treatment with medications, and we have explained the difference between an arrowhead that lodges in the kidney and one that lodges in the bladder, and all its signs, and we have mentioned the arrowhead where the operation is performed by hand and scalpel.
It is a special type of arrowhead that lodges in the bladder, and which gets stuck in the urethra, and I have described it with clear explanation and concise detail.
So I say that the arrowhead that lodges in the bladder is more likely to occur in children, and among its signs is that the urine comes out of the bladder like water in its clarity.
And gravel appears in it, and its mention is made, and it is painful for him, and often it becomes severe, then it subsides, and the symptoms appear with it, and many of them are troubled by it until they reach fourteen years, and it is more difficult for the old, while for the young, it is moderate between that.
And that which is a major arrowhead, its treatment is more difficult, and the small one is opposite to that. So if we turn to treatment, it is necessary first to make an incision in the perineum to extract all the gravel that is in its vicinity, for it may prevent the existence of the arrowhead when examining.
Then the perineum is taken with forceps, and it is pulled down to make the arrowhead descend to the neck of the bladder or to a raised position several times, then it is placed between your hands in a standing position, and its edges are under your thighs to incline the entire bladder downwards, then it is examined.
If you feel a sensation of numbness in the space, quickly move your finger over it. If it does not fall under your fingertips, it is likely that you will touch the inner finger with the edge of your left hand, if the patient is a young boy or the middle finger.
If it is a boy, insert it into his hip and feel for the numbness until it falls under your finger. Move it slightly towards the joint of the thigh, then grasp it with your finger and push it outwards towards the place you want to make an incision.
And order one of the attendants to hold the thigh with his hand, and order another attendant to stretch out his right hand above and his other hand to stretch the skin that is below the groin area near the place where the incision will be. Then take the scalpel, which has this shape.
And make the incision between the hip and the groin, not in the middle but towards the left side of the ailment, and let the incision be on the same numbness, with your finger in the hip, and you press it outwards, making the incision from outside wide and from inside as narrow as possible to allow the numbness to exit from it.
Do not make the incision too wide, lest you press the finger that is in the hip on the numbness during the incision, so it comes out with difficulty. And be aware that there may be numbnesses that have corners and hooks that make their exit difficult.
And among them is a numbness that resembles a bladder and is adherent, making its exit easy. But if it has corners and hooks, you increase the incision slightly, and if it does not come out thus, it is likely that you will need to dissect around it, or grasp it with a forceps that has a curved end like a Mibrad.
Grasp the numbness firmly so you do not drop it, or insert a delicate instrument with a curved end under it. If you cannot control it, widen the incision slightly, and if you have collected some blood, stop it with a dressing.
If there is more than one, then push the larger one towards the opening of the anus, and make an incision in it, then push the smaller one afterwards. And do likewise if there are more than two. If it is very large, then it is not possible to make a large incision in it, because it may cause damage to the surrounding area.
Either he dies or he will have a persistent urinary incontinence, because the passage will not adhere to its original place. But try to push it out until it emerges or is diverted into the perineum until it is completely emptied.
When you have finished your operation, sprinkle the wound with kost, and apply a compress, and bandage it firmly, and place over it a dressing soaked in oil or vinegar and rose-water. The patient should not move or bend for three days, and the bandage should not be removed until the third day.
If the wound has been washed with water and a great deal of oil, and treated with sweet aromatics and basil, until it heals, but if there is an appearance of inflammation in the wound, or burning pain, and such like, as if blood had clotted in the anus and urine was retained, and it is recognized by the emergence of blood with the urine.
So insert your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will cause putrefaction of the anus and its destruction. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt, and apply all kinds of treatment until it heals.
And it is necessary, during the treatment periods, to bind the thighs together and constrict them so that the medicines can be applied to the affected area. For if the hernia is small and has entered into the canal of the penis and has obstructed the urine from exiting, treat it with what I have described before, until it becomes ripe for incision.
Many times I have avoided making an incision because of this treatment, for it is more beneficial. It involves taking a scalpel made from the iron of a file, which has this shape:
Like a sharp-pointed instrument in the vein, then take a thread and tie it beneath the rib to prevent it from slipping back into the artery, then insert the cannula into the vessel through the incision until it reaches the said rib.
And insert the cannula into the rib slowly, slowly, and you pierce it until it reaches the other side, then the urine starts to flow from its orifice. Then, place your hand on what remains of the rib from outside the vein, for it will be severed and come out with the urine, and the patient will recover.
If this treatment does not work for you, and the stricture obstructs you from that, then tie a thread beneath the rib and another above the rib, then make an incision on the rib in the same vein between the two ligatures, then remove it.
Then release the ligature and clean the stagnant blood that has accumulated in the wound. And it is necessary to tie the thread beneath the rib so that it does not return to the artery, and the other ligature from above, so that when the thread is released after the removal of the rib, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound.
Therefore, it is necessary for you, when you tie the upper thread, to elevate the skin above so that it returns to its place and covers the wound as we mentioned.
The Sharp Instrument and the Stomacher.
For the removal of the rib in women.
It is rare for the rib to be inflamed in women, because if one of them suffers from a rib injury, it is difficult to treat her and many obstacles arise, one of which is that the woman may be modest and another is that you do not find a woman who would allow herself to be examined by a doctor.
If she is shy or one of those who are mahram (unmarriageable kin), and thirdly that you do not find a woman who is skilled in this craft, nor does she have the dexterity to perform it with her hand, and fourthly that the location of the incision on the rib in women is far from the location of the rib, so it requires a deeper incision.

Here is the translation:

And insert your finger, not deviating from the area, pressing underneath it; let the incision be small at first, then enter the probe through that small incision; if you feel around the area, increase the incision according to what you learn, that is, as much as you understand that the abscess will exit from it; and know that there are many types of abscesses.
Some are small and some are large, and there are smooth and rough ones, long and curved ones, and those with branches; so recognize their types to guide yourself on what you want, for if the blood overflows, let it flow in the elevated position, and squeeze it for an hour until the bleeding stops, then return to your work.

The Second and Sixth Operations.
On the incisions on the watery glands.
The watery glands are where moisture collects in the white fascia beneath the skin of the testicle surrounding the epididymis, and it is called the spermatic cord, which has a special membrane with a natural tendency towards one side of the testicle.
It may be thought that it is another testicle and it is between the skin of the testicle and the white fascia, which we have mentioned, but that is not so except in the case of a hernia, and these glands are generated from weakness that occurs in the anthelia, so this material collects in them, and they may be affected by a blow on the anthelia.
And this moisture has many colors, either it is yellowish, or it is reddish and bloody, or it is dark and blackish, or it is whitish and watery, which is what it is most of the time, and these are the signs by which it is recognized.
Where the water collects, if it is in the white fascia which we have mentioned, then the tumor becomes slightly elongated in shape like a testicle and the epididymis does not appear because the moisture surrounds it on all sides.
And if the moisture is in a special membrane belonging to it, then the tumor becomes elongated towards one side of the testicle.
And for this reason, the person thinks it is another testicle. And if the moisture is between the skin of the epididymis and the white fascia, then it falls under the sensation, and if you want to know the color of the moisture, then press the tumor with the flat, broad instrument that I have described its shape, and what comes out after pressing with the instrument will show you what is inside.
So if we resort to treatment with the iron, it is necessary to order the patient to sit on a couch with his back slightly raised and place many cloths under him, then you sit on his left side.
The surgeon sits comfortably on the left side of the patient, extending his hand to one side of the groin area and towards the umbilical region, then he takes a wide incision and dissects the spermatic cord from the middle all the way up to near the navel.
He directs the incision along a straight line parallel to the cord that divides the spermatic cord into two halves until it reaches the white linea alba, then he extracts it and takes care not to cut too much, and it becomes clear to him from the side that adheres to the testicle more, and he extracts as much as possible.
Then he opens the full and wide aponeurosis, and drains all the fluid, then he separates the edges of the incision with sponges and elevates the aponeurosis upwards without touching the cord containing the testicle, and he cuts the aponeurosis as much as you can, either by a single cut or by multiple small cuts.
And do not neglect his thin side, for if you did not extract the cord completely, you would not be safe from the fluid returning; so if you have brought the testicle out of its sheath while operating, then when you finish cutting the aponeurosis, return it to its place and reunite the edges of the spermatic cord with sutures.
Then he should treat the rest of the surgical wounds until he recovers, for if the testicle has become gangrenous due to another disease, it is necessary to ligate the vessels in the cord to prevent bleeding, then cut off the spermatic cord from the cord and extract the testicle, and treat him as we have mentioned.
If the fluid has accumulated in both sides, then know that there are two hernias, so dissect the other side as you did with the first one, and if it is possible for you to make it a single operation, do so, then wipe away the blood.
And he inserts into the incisions a pad that has been soaked in oil or rose-water, and places another pad that has been soaked in sherbet and oil outside, and applies it to both testicles and umbilical region, and puts on top a wrapped dressing, which is the bandage. And tie it from above with the bandage that has six flaps according to this figure:
Then take two pieces of cloth, and cut and shape them according to this example, making the flaps that are attached to it from cotton or moistened wool, and gather them in a sash at the waist, and one of the flaps takes hold of the shoulder-blade towards the back.
And the second (flap) takes towards the armpit, and the two flaps on the thighs from below, and the two remaining flaps on the hips, and gather all of it in a sash at the waist. You can also make this bandage with thread instead of stitching with iron.
And take a gentle, curved scalpel to dissect the peritoneum, and it is suspended on what we have described until the white shiny peritoneum is exposed for containing water, then take another scalpel on this figure:
It resembles the Greek incision, then you will open it and suspend that peritoneum until all the fluid comes out, then you will extend the peritoneum with the hooks and dissect the layer containing it with the scalpel and cut it according to what is possible for you until you remove it all and beware of the ureter so that you do not touch it with the scalpel.
Be aware that this operation is more subtle and farther from bleeding, and better than working with stitching, for if you encounter a problem in the stitching or during the thread, or inflammation or bleeding or something else, it is necessary to treat every problem that arises from that with the treatment that suits it according to what has been mentioned.
If the patient was weak and did not tolerate this operation due to its difficulty, then do not persist in it, but rather work according to what I have described, and if it is correct with you, then follow what we have mentioned from the signs.
Since the bandage is watery, it is necessary to seat the patient on a high chair, then open the tumor at its base with a narrow incision, and put the bandage along the length of the body, making the opening wide enough to drain all the water, then place a compress on the site and bind it.

When you need to enter the wound with a scraper or a dilator, it is essential to extract the pus that has accumulated and formed its shape, or add slightly to the opening of the wound.
And know that the pus may return and collect after six months or so, for if it collects, then treat it in the same manner and ward off the illness from it.
Chapter Three and Sixty.
On the incision of the muscular wounds and their treatment.
Know that the incision on these muscles is one of the most damaging things leading to destruction in most cases, so we see abandonment and avoidance of it, and I warn against operating on them and the types of gangrene.
So I say that many ulcers have occurred on the bodies that are composed of putrid matter and that is due to many causes, either from a corrupt humor that flows to the affected part or from a blow, and the color of the ulcer is like the color of the body and does not have pus.
And the ulcer is putrid, and perhaps the ulcer was congealed in its color like wax and had no sensation, and it may be due to the obstruction of the veins and their inflammation, as has been mentioned before, or from the inflammation of the arteries, so what was from the obstruction of the veins is recognized by the spreading of the ulcer.
If you compress it with your fingers, and it is not suitable to expose it to the lancet, and as for what is due to inflammation of the arteries, nothing spreads from it when compressed with the fingers, and this type can be incised upon, like other muscles.
And it is that you incise the aponeurosis of the lumbar region, then extend the periosteal elevator to above and extract it from the white fascia, and free the ligament from the vessels, and ligate the vessels, and cut the ligament after freeing it from every side of the sides of the periosteum, for if the periosteum has adhered to those inflamed tissues.
You should extract the egg and cut it, and if there is adhesion between some of the fasciae or in what is between the vessels, you should release all that adhesion and cut it with a straight incision.
If the flesh has grown in the place of adhesion which is behind, you should cut all of it and extract the egg as we mentioned. If you have completed your work, wash the wound with warm rose-water and olive oil, then treat it with a gentle treatment until it heals.
Chapter Four and Sixty.
On the Treatment of Hernias that are accompanied by Ulcers.
Ulcers are festering wounds that resemble abscesses, accompanied by relaxation of the anus, and difficulty in the movement and exercise of the bowel, and in the treatment of this ailment from the nearest external [treatment] which we have previously mentioned.
But it is necessary to mention the work involved in it, as the ancients have done, so I say that you should sit the patient on an elevated chair, then push the buttocks downwards, and grasp the testicles with your fingers along with the vessels that are close to the penis.
And let another servant hold them firmly, and press them with a strong pressure, then make an incision with a sharp instrument, making a curved cut around the vessels until they are exposed, and then dissect from every side as I mentioned to you in the section on the surgical procedures for the varicose veins in the limbs, and then insert a thread into the needle.
And tie it at the first places that were affected by the ulcer, and also tie it at its end, then make a longitudinal incision in the middle, following the length of the patient's body, and extract what has accumulated in it from the purulent and corrupt matter.
Then treat the wound with a treatment similar to other surgical treatments that you want to perform for a period of time to remove the vessels that nourish one of the buttocks, and there is no harm in that, because if the ulcer has affected all the vessels, it is necessary to extract one of the buttocks along with the vessels so that the egg-shaped mass does not receive nourishment. Before cutting the vessels, they should be ligated so that they do not bleed excessively.
The Fifth and Sixth Sections.
On the treatment of wandering abscesses.
These abscesses occur from a rupture that appears in the descending peritoneum of the abdomen, near the umbilical region, and the pus flows from that rupture to one of the flanks.
And this rupture is either from a perforation of the peritoneum or from its extension, and these two types occur due to various causes, such as a blow, a fall, a thrust, lifting something heavy, and so on. And if it occurs due to an extension of the peritoneum, it will happen gradually over a long period of time.
And it does not happen suddenly, and the tumor is flat and towards the depth before the peritoneum becomes inflamed and pus forms, and if it occurs due to a perforation of the peritoneum, it happens from the beginning with severe pain and the tumor is varied and visible under the skin near the umbilical region.
And that is by the exit of the pus and its direction to the outside from the peritoneum, and it may come out with the pus and blood, thus these abscesses are called wandering and biliary, and they may be accompanied by a fetid smell, and the pus may penetrate into the peritoneal cavity and settle there, resulting in the destruction of the adjacent tissue.
Because it causes severe pain and distress, and it is not trivial if it becomes chronic. The treatment of these types of abscesses is very dangerous and requires great caution to avoid falling into it. The method of action is to instruct the patient to push the pus back into its cavity with his fingers, if possible, for a quick recovery.
Then he should lie on his back between your hands and raise his legs, then stretch the skin that is near the umbilical region upwards and make an incision in the entire length of the skin of the affected area, then insert sutures at the edges of the incision according to what is needed to open it.
The incision should be according to the extent that the egg can come out of it, then you should free the membranes underneath the skin of the thigh until when the white solid fascia appears from every direction, then you should insert your finger into what is above the egg.
In what is between the white fascia that is underneath the skin of the egg and the second fascia, and you release the adhesion that is behind the egg, then you bend with your right hand into the thigh's skin and with this you extend the white fascia above with your left hand and raise the egg with its fascia towards the direction of the incision.
And you order the servant to extend the egg upwards and release the adhesion that is behind, releasing it completely, and you feel with your finger so that there is nothing from the tangled fatty tissue in the white solid fascia, for if you find something of it, you should push it down towards the abdomen below.
Then you take a needle with a thick thread that is made of ten threads, and you insert it at the end of the fascia that is underneath the skin of the thigh near the incision, then you cut the edges of the twisted thread until they become four threads. Then you assemble some of them on each other in a woven shape and tie the fascia that we mentioned is underneath the skin of the thigh with a strong bond from two directions, then you also twist the edges of the threads and tie them with a strong tie until nothing of the vessels that nourish it can reach it. So that it does not protrude and become a painful tumor, and also becomes a second bond outside the first bond, distant from it by less than two fingers, and after these two bonds, you remove from the fascia underneath the skin of the thigh as much as the bone of the finger.
So that it does not protrude and become a painful tumor, and also becomes a second bond outside the first bond, distant from it by less than two fingers, and after these two bonds, you remove from the fascia underneath the skin of the thigh as much as the bone of the finger. And you cut the rest of it circularly and remove the egg with it, then you make a shallow incision in the thigh's skin to let out the blood and pus as we described previously, then the soaked lint is used with oil and placed on the wound, and the bond that we described is used.
When the white tender skin is cut, and a small part of it is removed to release the blood, it often happens that this is exposed, and the bandage is left until it falls off by itself. Then the abscess forms and collects what is discharged, until it ruptures with the foul pus.
Then the wound is treated with a sharp treatment of incisions until it heals.

Chapter 7 and 60.
On the fracture that occurs in the ribs.
The fracture may occur in the ribs, as we mentioned, in a certain position, and it does not descend to the inner cavities with anything of the pus, and if it descends, that is slight, and it returns at all times.
But if the fracture is delayed, the incision in the ribs increases until the pus and the abscess descend to the loin, and this occurs due to the extension of the fracture that occurs in the ribs, as we mentioned. And that is why it extends to the rib, and then it relaxes and fills the position, and its treatment is by cauterization, as we have described and explained.
And it may be treated with iron in this way: the patient is laid on his back between your hands, then the position of the fracture is opened with a transverse incision about three fingers' breadth, and the ribs underneath the skin are ligated.
When you expose the white fascia that is underneath, take a compress and place it on the site of the fascia, and then press it onto the depth of the abdomen. Then, you stitch the two sites together using the compress, and attach one to the other with sutures.
Then, you release the edge of the compress, and do not cut the entire fascia, nor touch the bladder, or anything else, as I have instructed you in the treatment of abdominal wounds. Then, you treat them with surgical treatments.
If the sutures are cut, clean them and close the wound until it heals, for the fascia will contract and not increase in size.
And it is better to make the incision at this site because it is closer to the safety.
Chapter 8 and 60.
Relaxation of the spermatic cord.
Many times, the spermatic cord relaxes in some people without relaxing the ligaments that are inside it, and its appearance becomes distorted. Therefore, whoever desires to treat it should place a poultice on his back.
And he should cut all the relaxed cord from the thick cord, then bring the edges together. And if you desire to suture, first suture the relaxed cord with three or four stitches, and tighten them well, then cut what is between the sutures.
Then treat it with other surgical treatments until he recovers and the sutures fall off.
Chapter 9 and 60.
On cauterization.
Cauterization is prohibited in our Sharia.
Therefore, it was not fitting for me to mention it in this book of mine, but I mentioned it for two reasons: one is that it should be known by the physician if he is asked about it, so he may know how to treat whoever is afflicted with it; and the other reason is that we often need to cauterize some animals for our benefit.

Here is the translation:
When you have exposed the testicles, separate them after having dissected them, and do not leave any of the membranes on them except for the delicate membrane that is on the vessels, and this type of dissection is better than that which is done with the scalpel.
For the scalpel might leave something of the anthela in the living being, then it treats the wound until it heals.
Chapter 67.
Treatment of Hemorrhoids.
Hemorrhoids occur in men in two types, one of which appears as a swelling in the perineum or in the groin area between the thighs, resembling a woman's vulva with hair, and it may obstruct urination from what is in the groin area.
And in women, there is one type, which occurs above the vulva on the perineum, like small, projecting buttons, coming out from one of them as if it were a man's penis, and the two are like the thighs. And the treatment for these three types.
The two types in men and the one type in women require that those excessive growths be excised until their effect is removed, then they are treated with other treatments for wounds until they heal. But as for the second type in men, which involves urinary obstruction from what is in the groin area, there is no operation for it, nor is there any protrusion of buttons.
Chapter 68 and 67.
On the excision of the clitoris and the projecting flesh from the vulva of women.
The clitoris may increase in size due to natural causes until it becomes erect and its appearance is disfigured, and it may grow in some women until it resembles that of men and reaches sexual intercourse.
It is necessary to grasp the base of the clitoris with your fingers or with a pincer and excise it, without hesitating in the cutting and not being anxious about the depth of the root, so that bleeding does not occur.
Here is the translation:
A return to outside on the example of the ulcer. Therefore, some of the ancient physicians called it a ulcerous disease, and they thought that it should be cut out like a gangrenous limb, and treated until it heals.
Chapter 27.
On the Treatment of Hemorrhoids.
Hemorrhoids are when the woman's anus is not perforated or the hole is small, and it can be either natural, born with it, or acquired, and the acquired one occurs due to a previous illness, which is either from an emerging bloody vein.
It can be a thin or thick vein, and it can be either in the depth of the womb or in its sides or at its top or bottom, and it is obstructed by intercourse, pregnancy, and childbirth, and sometimes by menstruation, and knowing that is done by examination through the vagina.
If the obstruction appears near, and it does not appear, then touch it with your fingers or with a rod; if the obstruction is from a thin vein and it is near the lips, then make an incision, which is to create on the lips something like a pustule, then place all your fingers of both hands.
And the woman should be on her back, with her legs apart, then she should stretch out her lips strongly until the thin vein is cut, and the obstruction opens up, then take a swab, dip it in oil, and apply it to the site, and compress the woman every day so that the site does not close again.
If the vein is thick and dense, it should be cut with a sharp scalpel like a thin paper, if the obstruction is from an emerging bloody vein, then ligate it with threads, and cut it off, and have with you medicines that stop the bleeding without being painful, such as white lead, and chamomile, and others.
A tube of wide copper is used to drain the wound quickly, and it is held in place by a bandage, then a piece of cloth is applied to absorb the discharge, and treatment with a poultice is continued until healing occurs, for it may be necessary to cut on this pattern.
What has not been cauterized by the copper tube, if it is a cancerous tumor that is in the womb, it cannot be treated with branding iron.
Chapter Three and Seventy.
On the treatment of ulcers, sores, and red swellings that occur on the vulva of women.
As for ulcers, it is an inflammation of the vessels of the arteries until a lot of blood flows from them constantly, and if the ulcer becomes chronic, it turns into sores. We have mentioned in the chapter on anatomy their types, symptoms, and we will mention them here.
What can be treated and what cannot be treated, so I say that ulcers and sores, if they are deep in the womb and do not reach the sensation, there is no treatment with branding iron, and whatever is on the surface of the womb can be felt, it is those that can be treated.
It is necessary for the woman to enter a cold room, then to extend the sores with a scraper or a rough cloth and to cut them off from their roots, then to apply something to stop the flow of blood from one of the cutting veins without cauterizing.
Like aloe, and chamomile, and plantain, and their like, then lift her legs to the wall for an hour, then let them down in cold water, if the bleeding persists, sit her on a mattress of samak, and pomegranate peel, and walnut, and their like, then take a fine powder of barley, and make it into a paste with honey and vinegar.
And apply it to her back, if the bleeding stops, or else, apply a solid plaster to the sides and breasts without harshness, then take a swab of cotton, and dip it in the juice of the Tartarath, or the juice of the pregnant woman's milk, or the juice of the pomegranate, with a mixture of walnut and rose-water, and apply it to the affected area.
If the patient is troubled by a tumor at the affected site, treat it with the corresponding medicine until he recovers. As for the red swelling, it resembles an erysipelas rash, rough to the touch and unpleasant to look at; one should excise what appears of it according to what I mentioned in the chapter on ulcers, and treat it until he recovers.
Chapter 47.
On the Abscess That Appears in the Womb.
It may appear in the womb various kinds of tumors, such as cancer, and the ulcerated tumor, and the abscesses, and the festering, and the apostemes, and the gangrenous, and the phlegmonous, and the hemorrhoids, and the ulcers. I have mentioned all these diseases and their types and signs in the classification.
We should mention in this chapter the inflammatory tumor that appears in the womb, if it is one of those tumors that gather gradually, how to treat it with iron, we should examine whether the pain of the tumor was severe from its beginning, with fever and inflammation.
And its appearance is red, if the sensation falls upon it, do not hasten to treat it, and deal with it gently by what is beneficial for the humor, until when these symptoms settle, then it is time to make the woman sit on a chair with a cushion under her, and lean back against it.
And gather her legs towards the lower abdomen, and let her thighs be apart, and direct her feet underneath her hips, and bind them with a bandage that is suitable.
Then, have the woman sit on the side of her right hip, and use the instrument that opens up to insert into the womb, whose shape will be described later. And it is necessary, if you want to use this instrument, to measure the depth of the woman's womb beforehand, so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the womb.
If the instrument was longer than the depth, it is necessary to place a rest on the shaft of the instrument for the sake of facilitating its entry into the depths of the wound, and it is necessary to bend the loop that is inserted through the instrument from the upper side.
And you hold the instrument and the servant turns the loop until it opens into the wound, so if the abscess appears and is touched by the hand and is thin in its base, it is necessary to incise it at its head with a narrow scalpel, so if the entire duration is spent.
It is necessary to make a thin, curved incision in the wound, hidden in the flesh of the wound or with green olive oil, including some compression, and the incision will be outside the wound at the neck of the womb, and it will be from the outside on the womb and on the peritoneum, a thin, curved suture in water that has been cleansed with khabazi.
Then treat afterwards with the beneficial remedies that are suitable for it, until he recovers.
And it is possible to wash the womb and the wound with water and honey, then with water that has been cleansed with the juice of the Suse or Zurunad for a long time, then return to the remedies, if the abscess was scattered internally in the womb.
It is necessary to refrain from treating it with iron, but rather treat it with what we have mentioned in the previous section.
Chapter 55 and 56.
On teaching about the treatment of living organs, how they are treated if they deviated from their natural shape.
It is necessary for the practitioner to know the first natural shape of birth, and from its signs, if you see a woman leaning forward towards the bottom and stretching to breathe in deeply and relaxing what is upon her from the pains.

If it has descended onto his head, the afterbirth will come out with it and be cleared of those remnants in a good clearing, but this birth is not natural because the fetus may emerge on its knees and bring out its hands before its head and knees.
And it may bring out one arm or one leg, or emerge headfirst or in a bent position, and perhaps turn around on its axis, and so on of those abnormal forms. Therefore, it is necessary for the accoucheur to be gentle with these things all and avoid mistakes and errors.
And we have explained each shape of them and how the trick is in it, so you can deal with it and stop it. If the fetus emerges headfirst, which is the natural exit, and it puts pressure on the woman, making delivery difficult for her and weakening her strength, then I sit her down on a cushion and instruct the women to hold her firmly.
