If it does not come down, then it is necessary to apply a warm compress to the woman with melted fat of the deer, and then instruct her after the application to move around and shake herself with the cushion and hold her mouth and nose, for the fetus will come out in its time. If the fetus' hand emerges first, then it is necessary to gently pull it little by little.
If it does not enter, then place the woman on a stool and raise her legs up high, then shake the stool on the ground while the woman holds onto it so as not to fall during the shaking. If the hands did not enter and the fetus died, then extract them and pull out the rest of the fetus.
And he will put his hands on her flaccid abdomen and feel it, and if the fetus emerges onto its feet, then you should push them upwards, then turn the fetus a little by little until it is upright, then take one of its feet and stretch it out a little by little.
And if it emerges onto the thighs, then order her to take a deep breath and contract her muscles strongly, for it will emerge. If it does not emerge as we have described, then turn the fetus a little by little until it takes its natural position, for then it will emerge slowly. If you are unable to do what we have described, then try everything.

Then insert it into the woman's genital area and lower part of her abdomen, then sit her in warm water until she reaches the point of delivery.
And if you see that it has not come down, then make her a warm drink and carry her. If she holds the drink for an hour, then sit her on the birthstool, then contract her muscles and close her mouth and nose, and press her lower abdomen with a gentle pressure, for the fetus will emerge at that hour, emerging onto its knees and hands.
If it emerges in this manner, then insert your hands little by little, and then make the woman lie on her back and spread her legs downwards while she is in a reclined position, and grasp her hands. If the fetus does not emerge, take both of its legs and shake them with a strong movement. Then press above the pubic area little by little until the fetus rises upwards. Then insert the hook and turn the fetus little by little.

Chapter Six and Seven.
On extracting a dead fetus.
If you treated the dead fetus with what was mentioned in the section on treatment and it did not come out, and you were forced to resort to manual operation, it is essential that you examine; if the woman was strong and healthy, and there was nothing among the symptoms that would make you fear a perforation, it is essential that you lay the woman on a couch on her back.

Chapter 79.
On the treatment of the uterus that has not been perforated.

The Eighty-Eighth Chapter.
On the Treatment of Ulcers that Occur on the Soles.
Ulcers that occur on the soles are a complication and hardness that occurs near the passage from outside or in the void from one of the directions, and the ulcer is one or more.
So if that complication becomes chronic, a white watery discharge or thin pus may issue from it, and it may be among those ulcers that penetrate to the marrow and to the surrounding area, and they may not be penetrating, for the penetrating ones are recognized by what is discharged from them of dung and flatulence when using the instrument of probing.
And sometimes worms may issue from it, and they may be among those ulcers that, if in the void, penetrate to the bladder and to the passage of the penis, and they may be among those that penetrate to the joint of the thigh and to the heel of the foot, and what is known about the ulcer that penetrates to the passage also differs from the non-penetrating one.
You insert your index finger into the passage and insert a thin probe into the ulcer from a copper or iron instrument, if there is no roughness in the ulcer; but if there is roughness, you insert a probe of silver or a thread from horsehair threads.
Until you feel with the probe or thread on your finger, and if you do not feel any roughness, and nothing of dung or flatulence or worms issues from the wound, as we said, then know that it is non-penetrating, so proceed to treatment.
If the fracture is extended to the bladder or to the ureter, it indicates that the urine will flow out of it and prevent it from being retained in its place by medication, and if it is extended to the joint of the thigh or to the ankle bone, it is marked by the arrival of the spar at that point.
If there is no abrasion to the bone and pus is present in a direction towards the site, and it constantly flows out, and there is no benefit from treatment, nor does it adhere to the limb, and all these fractures are non-unifying, so none of them will form a callus.
And its treatment is futile for whoever relies on it from the ignorant physicians, and as for those that are not extended and not complicated, I will describe the callus formation with the help of a solid structure, as I have experienced and tried, which is to place the splint between your hands on his back.
And you should raise his thigh above and bend his knee towards his belly, then insert the spar of iron or lead, if there is an abrasion in the fracture until it reaches where the spar ends, for you will feel the callus forming near the seat, so you should insert your fingers into the seat.
For if you feel with your fingers the spar has penetrated to its full extent, being hidden without your feeling it between your fingers and it by the skin or the flesh, then you will know that it is extended, so do not labor over it, for there will be no callus from it, as we have said.
And they have said that it heals in some people through the gentleness and from the treatment that is hoped to benefit, by applying a thin layer of wax according to the size of the fracture, as previously mentioned, and inserting it gently into the fracture until it reaches near the seat, then leaving it for two or three days.
Until you know that it has absorbed all those excess, attached, and redundant flesh that resembles a bird's pipe, then you treat it with a poultice of melted fat in the honey until those absorbed flesh comes out, then you treat it with sticky plaster, for it will heal.
If the wound does not heal with other treatments, and if the splint is inserted and does not reach the bone which is in the cavity, and there was a thick layer of flesh or membrane between them and the splint, I saw the abscess on the surface of the skin, so I incised the skin from the beginning of the abscess. And you continue with the incision along with the splint, which is in the abscess, until you reach the end of the splint with the incision, and then the splint is removed and drops out, then you clean those adherent membranes that resemble a bird's feather pipe, and nothing remains of them.
Then you treat it with soothing medications until it heals, for if the blood overcomes you and it is difficult for you to cut those membranes, it is better to do what you can do, and faster to benefit by cauterizing them with fire or a sharp medicine, because cauterizing with fire combines two good effects, removing those excess membranes.
And stop the bleeding and remove the blood clots, then treat it with rose water or borax powder mixed with oil, until the area becomes clean and those rotten membranes come out in the pus, then treat the wound at that time with soothing medications that promote the healing of solid flesh.
And these are the medications that contain astringent and stopping properties, for if they are applied, the wound will heal and not become inflamed again; if the abscess has reached the depth of the cavity and is far from the surface of the body, then insert your finger into the cavity and open it up.
For if you feel the splint and between it and your finger there is a membrane of flesh or skin, and it was close to penetrating, then the work on it would be only through the method of gentle touch and hope, that is, you use one of three ways, either you cauterize it as we mentioned.
If you do not cut until you reach the apex, to facilitate the insertion of the instrument and treatment from a distance, do not rely on cutting because it might sever the surrounding ligament at the joint, causing the prolapse of the intestine outside without intention. Then, treat it as we have mentioned, so that it may be repaired as we have said.
And if you perforate the peritoneum and make an incision after cutting near the joint as we have said, either with a sharp instrument or another sharp one at the edge, then clean out those adherent membranes that are in the incision, each to where it was necessary to dissect.
Then bring the edges of the wound together with the incision and the upper lip until they unite, and the noselike orifice remains open inside the joint, making it easier on the patient, although the noselike orifice may close in this way.

The Hundredth and Eighth Section.
On the excision of varicose veins, and their ligation, and treatment of ulcers.
Varicose veins occur on the limbs, either within the skin resembling red streaks or like a cluster of grapes, and they may be small or large, and blood flows from them continuously.
They may be single, or multiple, and they may be outside the skin, on its surface, but those that are outside the skin are mostly lacking in humidity, and a yellowish fluid or a little blood flows from them continuously, and they appear on the color of the skin.
And the treatment of those that are within the skin is to make an incision, and to dissect until the skin is exposed, and the varicose veins appear, then you ligate them with a thread or grasp them with a forceps, and then cut them off at their roots; if you do not ligate them with the thread due to their brittleness and fragility.
Then shave them with a rough razor or a piece of burnt rope, or grasp them with your fingers and then cut them, and apply some caustic remedies afterwards, to fulfill their purpose as a substitute for cauterization, or apply them according to what has been mentioned in the chapter on cauterization.
Then treat them with other treatments until they heal, but if the skin does not allow for their exit, then make a small incision in the skin to extract what is within it, and apply gentle pressure to expel them quickly when making the incision; thus, you will have removed the varicose veins that are outside the skin, and their treatment becomes easy.
And it is that you grasp them with forceps or ligate them with a thread and cut them, then treat them as we have mentioned until they heal; and if you are averse to cutting with a cautery iron, it is preferable to use a thread in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle.
Pass the thread through and tie it with a needle at its base from the other side, and wrap the end of the thread around the needle, which is opposite and tight. Then, tighten the thread strongly and pull out the needle, doing so for all the stitches, leaving one that you do not pull.
You extract a little of the blood, then you put on the affected area a piece of cloth dipped in rose water or iroutine, and you apply it to the affected area, and you bandage it with a compress, then you leave it until it falls off. If the stitches fall apart, you treat them with ointments and other treatments until they heal.
As for the treatment of fractures, it is often necessary to deal with the ugliness of the splint and the curvature of the bone. If it becomes inflamed and does not respond to medication, it may be necessary to scrape it with a scalpel or a rasp until it becomes smooth and the upper crust that prevents its union is removed.
Then you treat it until it adheres as desired, and if it does not adhere, you scrape it again with a stronger rasp than the first time, until it is formed well and is repaired. Then you treat it, and it heals.

It is necessary to make an incision around the hernia and grasp it with a forceps or a hook, and then to dissect from its base. Then you treat it, and if it is small, it is a minor, rough, inflamed, and protuberant swelling on the surface of the body.
What is frequently encountered in the treatment of wounds in children and its management, is to extend the sutures and cut them off or remove them with a thin thread or a hair until they fall out, and if you want to leave it as it is on the basis of what has been mentioned previously, either by cauterization or by medicated bandages.

It exists entirely in the body and its abundance is in the fingers, and its treatment is to take a tube made from the feather of a strong goose or eagle, and shape that tube around the scab until it forms a circle around it from all directions, then insert your hand with the tube until you dissect what surrounds the scab.

Chapter 84.
On the Treatment of Wounds.
I have mentioned in the chapter on treatment that I have discussed the treatment of similar wounds and I will discuss their treatment here with the hand and medications, according to completeness. So, I say that wounds differ according to the condition of the member in which the wound occurs and according to the location where the wound is situated.
The things that cause wounds are many, such as a hit with a stone or a cut with a sword or a dagger or a stab with a knife or a blow or a bite and so on from many things.
And wounds differ according to their locations on the body, such as a wound that occurs on the head or neck or chest or belly or liver and so on from the organs.
And I have described the treatment of some wounds to make them a model and a law for other wounds, and I began with simple head wounds specifically because the compound ones will be mentioned later in the third chapter of this book.
So I say that if a simple wound occurs on the head and does not involve a fracture of bone, you should examine it to see if it was caused by a hit with a stone or something similar, and it has only split the skin, and the wound is large and you fear the occurrence of a severe inflammation, then hasten and wash the scalp thoroughly. And do not delay it and extract from him as much blood as his strength allows, if it does not stop the bleeding, neither more nor less, for the blood that comes out of the wound is slight, and let the bleeding be from the opposite side of the affected area.
Beware of the patient with inflammation, and the intense heat, and the swollen veins, for if you neglect to treat him, his condition will worsen, and he will be unable to eat, and the swellings will increase, and it will lead to a severe ulcer with yellowish discharge in the wound or with the intense heat that has taken hold.
And if the severe ulcer is intense, then operate on the wound if it has become thin in its skin and the air has not penetrated to the place that I will describe to you soon, and if the air has penetrated to it, then operate with some of the remedies.

Chapter 85.
On Surgical Operations on the Abdomen and the Extraction of the Omentum and Its Suturing.
The hernia that appears on the abdomen may be large, or small, or medium; a large one may bring out omentum or several omenta, making their introduction and suturing more difficult and tiresome.
And the small hernia also may be difficult for another reason, in that it is necessary to return it with difficulty and the omentum, if you do not hasten to return it to its place from its hour of inflammation and swelling, making its return difficult. Therefore, it is better than the large hernia or the medium-sized one, because returning the omentum does not become difficult as it does in these two types.
And know that suturing the abdomen is in four ways: two general ways that are suitable for suturing the abdomen and other abdominal wounds, and two special ways that concern other wounds, except that they are more specific to suturing the abdomen.
And I will describe them to you one by one, with explanation and clarification. So I say that if the wound is small and a part of the omentum has come out and its return is difficult, then it is due to one of two reasons: either because the hernia is small, as we have mentioned, or because the omentum has become inflamed before the air was let in.
If it is thus, it is advisable to soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water and squeeze it out, then bind it with a bandage and tighten it until the swelling subsides.
And the erab which has a compressing quality is better than water alone in reducing the swelling, so if you find that the swelling has subsided, loosen the bandage with warm water in which a little of kammi or khubazi has been added, for it facilitates its insertion with gentle ease.
If the patient complains of return of the symptoms after this treatment, make a small incision in the skin with the instrument which makes the small incisions and repeat the first treatment, for it is better than making an incision and it will not be necessary to resort to incision except in cases of necessity and inability to bear the treatment.
The single curved forceps has one end limited and the other end not limited, and the delicate extremity is not firm in the grasp but is slightly flexible, and it resembles a small solj. As you see, if the wound gapes open and the bandage enters, it is advisable that it be returned to its natural shape.
And its specific position is better if it can be managed thus, and if the wound was wide and located on the lower abdomen, it is advisable to lie on his back with his legs elevated above his head, and if it was on the upper abdomen, he should elevate his head and chest above his lower parts.
And likewise, if the wound was on one side of the abdomen, you should always elevate the affected side, where the surgery is being performed, above the other side; and thus it is advisable to use this in major surgeries and in moderate ones.
And in minor surgeries, you should adjust it according to what is convenient for you, then prepare between your hands a gentle and moderate grip that holds the entire wound with his hand and brings its edges together, then uncovers it to apply the suture thread little by little.
This is the description of the simple suture, and it is that you take a needle or several needles according to the width of the wound, then leave from the edge of the skin an amount equivalent to the thickness of the knuckle, and insert one needle without putting thread in the edges of the skin. With the edges of the superficial fascia under the skin, from inside, you pierce them from that direction; and you have gathered the edges of the skin and the edges of the superficial fascia, and formed four stay sutures. Then, you tighten with a thread around the needle several times from both directions until the edges of the wound meet together perfectly.
Then, you leave an amount equivalent to the thickness of the finger as well, and insert another needle, then you sew it with the thread as you did with the first needle. Do not cease doing that until you complete the entire wound, and the needles are evenly spaced between the thickness and the thinness.
Because the thin needles are very sharp and cut through the flesh and the bones also, it is difficult to enter the skin. Therefore, it is necessary to be moderate in the thinness and the thickness, and it is not necessary to insert the needle at the edge of the skin too closely.
So that the flesh does not cut quickly and the wound does not open before it heals, and you do not tighten too much with the suture, so that the wound is not prevented from healing. Then, you cut the edges of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient when he moves and you make for him a dressing of two pieces of cloth from each side to hold the edges of the needles.
And you leave it until you know that the wound has healed, and this type of suture with needles is more beneficial in small surgeries because it can be sufficient to suture with one or two needles, or approximately.

Chapter 7 and 8.
On Cutting off Limbs and Setting Bones.
The limbs may become putrid either due to an external cause or an internal one. If you treated that putridness with medicinal treatment and it did not benefit from the treatment, and you saw the putridness spreading in the limb without anything stopping it.
It is necessary to amputate that limb to the point where the gangrene has reached, to rescue from death or from great pain, which is more significant than losing a limb. A sign of this is that the limb becomes black, until you think that it has been burned by fire.
Or it putrefies after the blackening, until that putrefaction reaches what is adjacent to that limb and takes hold of the entire body, so hasten its amputation. And likewise, if the cause of the gangrene is some creeping pest, such as a sea crab or a viper or a centipede and the like.
If the gangrene or pestilence is in a finger, then amputate the finger and do not delay, lest the gangrene spread to the hand. And likewise, if it has taken hold of the hand, then amputate it from the base of the arm, and do not delay, lest it spread until it takes hold of the upper arm.
And likewise, if it has taken hold of the upper arm, then amputate the upper arm at the elbow joint itself. If the gangrene has spread and reached towards the shoulder, do not amputate the entire shoulder, for that would be a deadly operation. Instead, try other treatments according to one's strength.
And likewise, do the same with the foot if gangrene has taken hold of the toes, amputate the toes at one of the joints. And if it has taken hold of the ankle, then amputate the leg with its bones, and if it has spread to the knee, then amputate the thigh at the knee joint.
And if the gangrene has reached above the knee, then there is no remedy except to resign oneself to fate and surrender the patient to death. And it is proper to amputate a limb or to sever it by tightening a ligature below the place where you want to amputate, and tightening another ligature above the place.
And you should apply one ligature below and another above, and then sever the flesh between the two ligatures with a sharp scalpel until the entire flesh is exposed. Then amputate or separate it. And it is necessary to place a compress of lint on all sides.
When you touch the vein at the correct site, it will be evident to the senses if there is an extra or inflamed vein; if bleeding occurs during your operation, stop the bleeding quickly by applying pressure or using some compressing sutures to constrict the blood flow, then return to treating it until it heals.
Then bind the injured limb with a bandage that suits it, and treat it until it recovers. I will give you an example of a case where a man suffered from this condition in his leg, which I described to you, and that is what happened to him: he had a black swelling on his leg with a burning pain resembling fire.
And that was the first corruption that occurred in his finger, until the man felt it all, so he began to move his hand away from himself when he saw the corruption spreading in the limb with intense pain and burning, which he used to feel at the joint, so he desisted.
Then, after a long time had passed for him, that corruption appeared to him in his left hand's fingers, so I treated it by applying a remedy that I carried on my hand, after cleaning the affected area, and the corruption did not spread, but rather began to move into the other fingers.
Until the corruption reached his hand, and I was forced to amputate it, so I applied a dressing on it from my experience in treating that condition, and I also feared for his death when amputating his hand, because the man's strength was failing, and he was about to leave for his hometown.
He informed me that he had only saved his hand by amputating it, and I told this story to serve as a warning about what happens from this type of disease, and to be a guide for those who suffer from it and take action against it.
Chapter 88.
On the treatment of abscesses and how to inject them with medications.
If an abscess forms in some of the fleshy parts and the abscess takes a long time to gather, then it bursts or ruptures and all that was in it from the pus empties out, leaving the site empty as if it were a vessel.
The fracture that has occurred and has not been properly set, and has not affected the bone, nor the nerve, nor the ligament, and from here it is deserving to be named 'hidden' and should not be called 'broken' unless its duration reaches a point where it affects the corruption in one of these organs.
So, it is called 'broken' or 'dislocated', and its treatment is to cut the entire fracture as it revolves, and it will not be named thus if it has occurred and become dislocated, and you are certain that it does not adhere to its position due to corruption.
For if you find that the fracture has adhered and the corruption has not reached that amount, and there is a thick piece of meat in the fracture, active with the needle, it is that you should look at the hidden (part) - if it was large and the pus that flows from it is abundant, then treat it with the Egyptian medicine.
Which is: vinegar, honey, and sugar, all of equal parts, mixed together in a vessel and cooked over the fire until the medicine dissolves, then you take what you need from it and mix it with water and honey, and apply it to the hidden (part) and bind it firmly, and leave the medicine on it for two hours.
Then, you extract it with the press, doing that every day until the hidden (part) is cleansed and the pus disappears. If this medicine does not work for you, take the ash of burnt pomegranate or the ash of burnt quince, and mix it with water.
Then, you massage it and apply it until you are certain that the hidden (part) has healed. If it does not heal with the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then treat it with a mixture of water and honey in which is mixed a small amount of powdered sugar.
Or, treat it with honey and wine, mixed together, because the property of honey is to cleanse and purify, and wine helps to hold the hidden (part) in place; and it will not be so unless the wine is of superior quality and strong. So, if you do that repeatedly and are certain that the hidden (part) has disappeared, then treat it with what nourishes the flesh.
As you take from the rhizome of the nasal bone and dissect it with a scalpel and a straight forceps or hook, while freeing it from some medications and the other nasal bones whose characteristics we have mentioned in the chapter on nasal bones, if the passage of the antrum is narrow and does not allow the insertion of the instrument.
Open it with the iron a little, or place a curved file in the Egyptian nose bone or the Suriyani nose bone until it expands, and also if the mouth is wide, gather its lips with the sutures and leave as much as the instrument can enter without excess.
And also, if the mouth from which the pus flows upwards to the top, split it in a lower place so that the pus flows down, because when the pus accumulates in the depth of the antrum, it prevents the flesh from growing.
If you cannot split the antrum downwards as you wish, then incline the instrument in a way that allows the pus to flow out easily according to what is visible to you, and make sure that no part of the pus remains.
As for the medications that are applied to the antrum from outside and how they are placed on it, it is that you take one of the medications that are suitable for what you want and spread it on a piece of cloth, and let the cloth be as large as the antrum covers it entirely. Then you make an incision with the scissors in front of the mouth of the antrum, a little wider than the mouth of the antrum, then spread some of the soft medications on another piece of cloth according to the size of the incision and place it on it in a way that is away from the mouth of the antrum to facilitate the exit of the pus and do not remove the large piece of cloth until afterwards.
For several days, and as for what is on the mouth of the antrum, it is what you remove at every time to let out what has accumulated in it of pus, and to know what flows from it of discharge, whether it is much or little, thick or not thick.
With this, you should also examine the site of the abscess itself: does its owner feel pain in it, or is there no pain in it, and is there a swelling or is there no swelling? If you have treated it in this way and seen the purulent matter that comes out slowly from the site of the abscess.
You should know that the abscess has adhered or nearly adhered, so then you should open it on the fifth day or on the third day, and when you have opened the wound, replace the dressing with another and renew the medication. For if pus comes out of the abscess after a long period, it will be thin and clear, so do not despair at the suppuration.
You should drain it quickly, because some people delay the healing of the flesh in their wounds and contradict that. For if pus comes out of the abscess after many days without being thick, you should know that the abscess has not matured, so the suppuration of the abscess is delayed.
And treat his condition by strengthening the medicaments and make the medicaments be in their thick consistency and in their thinness like the Nakhliyah ointment, if it has been strengthened with the addition of Quqlqtar. And most informative of what is treated with is that the Nakhliyah ointment should be taken.
And apply the lead ointment and sprinkle on it the attar of roses, which is mixed with its thick consistency, then bandage it with it and use it. And you may do like this deed if you do not have the Nakhliyah ointment, honey, or rose-water, even if you take from the bitter and aloe and colocynth and grind them all together and apply it to the sore while it is on fire. Then apply it to the dressing and bind it to the abscess, or smear it with honey that has been cooked until it thickens, and put the medications on it and apply the dressing, binding it.
Here is the translation:
A fracture in the bone or in other solid organs or ligaments requires treatment according to what is presented.
Chapter 89.
On the treatment of gout and ulceration, and cutting off the excess fingers and splitting of the nails.
Gout is a plentiful humor that grows under the nail of the finger or toe, and sometimes grows in other fingers, so if its matter increases and its treatment is neglected, it becomes swollen and painful.
Or it becomes putrid and rotten until it eats into the root of the nail, and sometimes it corrupts all of it, and sometimes the corruption reaches the bone, so that it has a foul smell and the tip of the finger becomes swollen and its color becomes dark blue, so if you treated it with what we mentioned in the section and the treatment did not succeed.
Then it is necessary to cut off with an iron all the putrid matter that grows from the nail, and then to cauterize the wound afterwards; indeed, cauterization in this case is very beneficial, provided the bone is sound and the nail is also sound.
And the corner of the nail fold had pushed the flesh inside and made it swollen and painful, so it is necessary to put a thin probe under the corner of the nail that has pushed the flesh and lift it up, and then cut off that flesh gently.
And apply to the remaining flesh from the corrosive medicines that eat away until it disappears completely, then treat it with ointments until it heals; and if the corruption had affected the bone, it is necessary to cut out that bone and extract it, for it will not heal as long as there is rotten bone.
For if you see the putridity and corruption spreading in the fingers, cut them off at one of the joints as mentioned previously, then treat them until they heal; for if the nail is struck or bruised and a severe pain occurs, it is necessary to open the abscess first.
Cut the nail with a sharp instrument, inclining it from above to below, and be careful not to reach the flesh underneath the nail, lest you cause pain and severe injury to the patient. This will lead to excessive bleeding in the affected area.
And as for the extra fingers that grow on some people's hands, sometimes they are fleshy, sometimes they have bones, and sometimes they have nails, and their growth is rooted in the joint of some fingers.
And their growth is in some of the finger's joints, and what grows on some of the finger's joints does not move, and what grows at the joint of the finger sometimes moves; if it is just a fleshy piece, it is easy to cut it off at its base with a sharp instrument.
And as for those that grow at the base of the joint, it is difficult to treat them, so you should refrain from cutting them. And as for those that grow on the fingers at one of the joints, it is necessary to cut the flesh in a straight line up to the bone, and then scrape the bone with one of those suitable instruments.
Then treat until it heals, and as for the adhesion that occurs between some of the fingers, it is frequent that this happens and it is something that is born with humans, and it occurs when a wound or burn or similar injury occurs; it is necessary to separate those adhered parts.
Until the fingers return to their natural shape, then put between them a soft cloth or a piece of leather anointed with rose oil so that they do not adhere quickly and separate from each other, or make between them a thin sheet of copper, until the area is as it should be.
And likewise, if adhesion occurs between some of the fingers and the palm, then separate that adhesion according to what is needed, and repair it in a way that suits the shape of the limb.
The Ninetieth Chapter.
On the excision of the veins.
The veins are many, varicose, and full of bloody fluid, occurring in most parts of the body, but more frequently in the legs; it often happens in the thighs, calves, and hams. It is necessary to use the excision of the swollen vein from the black skin several times with strong excision.
Then the doctor treats it with iron, and its treatment is by cauterization, which has two effects: one is that it makes an incision and lets out black blood, and the other is that it seals the vein and lets out its putridity; but making an incision is on this condition, to drain the leg first with warm water.
Until the thick blood is dissolved, then the doctor should tighten the bandage around the leg from above its wound to its ankle with a wrapping, then make an incision in one place or two places or three separate incisions.
Then he should drain the black blood with his hands from the bottom of the leg to the top, and from the top to the bottom, until he removes as much blood as he thinks is sufficient or what the strength of the patient allows; then he should bandage it and order him to take nourishing food for the black skin, and to avoid puking and bleeding.
When the veins are full and that harms the patient, and its treatment is on this condition: to shave the doctor's leg if it has much hair, then to immerse it in warm water until it becomes hot and the vein opens or a strong sweating occurs.
If he does not immerse it in warm water until the member becomes hot, then he should make a longitudinal incision on the skin opposite the vein, either at the top near the knee or at the bottom near the ankle, and then open the skin with scissors and extract the vein from every direction until it becomes visible to the sense.
When it appears, you see a red vein, and when it is freed from the flesh, you see it as if it were a gut. Then, you insert a probe until, if it rises and exits the flesh, you tie it with a strong, smooth ligature. Then, you make another incision near that one, about three fingers in length.
Then, you strip the flesh from around the artery until it appears, then you elevate it with a probe as you did before, and tie it with another ligature as you did previously. Then, you make another incision or several incisions if you need to do so.
Then, you dissect it and cut it at the end of the incision near the ankle, then you pull it out until it exits from the second incision, then you pull it to the incision above it and do that until you pull it out from the third incision above all of them until, if its entirety emerges, you cut it.
If it does not respond to pulling and dissecting, then you insert a strong thread into the needle and tie it, and pull it out, and insert a probe underneath and manipulate it with your hand in every direction until it emerges, taking care not to cut it. If it gets cut, it will be troublesome for you to dissect it afterwards.
And you insert a dressing on the affected area, and if you dissected it all, then put a medicated poultice on the site of the incisions, made with rose oil or zit, and bandage it until it heals. If the diseased artery was twisted and had windings to its sides, that would be the case.
And do not be on a straight path as we mentioned, but rather make incisions on it at every direction of its windings and twistings, then tie it with ligatures until you dissect it entirely. And take care when making an incision on it not to cut the artery or pierce it, for that would be troublesome for you to dissect afterwards.

In the extraction of the median vein
This vein is generated in the legs in hot climates, such as Hijaz and Arab lands, and in hot climates with little hair and slight moistness, and maybe it generates in other places of the body besides the legs, and its generation occurs due to an inflammation that happens under the skin.
As it happens in the living bodies, and the lice, and the abscesses, and the generated swellings between the skin and the flesh. And the sign of the beginning of this vein is that it happens in the leg with severe inflammation, then the place becomes swollen, then the vein begins to emerge from that swelling.
It is as if it were the root of a plant or an animal, so if its tip appears, it should be wrapped with a small piece of lead that weighs from one dirham to two dirhams, and tied, and the lead is left suspended from the leg.
Whenever something emerges from it to the outside, wrap it in lead and tie it, for if you leave it, it will spread and cut some of it, and wrap the rest, do not cut it from its root before it all emerges, because if you cut it, it will constrict and enter the flesh, causing putrefaction and inflammation in the place, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore, it should be treated and drawn out little by little until it emerges completely, and nothing of it remains in the body. It is possible that from this vein, in some people, there may emerge five or ten finger-lengths.
It did not reach me that a man had an incision of twenty fingers, so I waited until you treated him, then I inserted a bandage into the wound and pressed it with a compress for a long time until all the putrid matter was evacuated from it, and I helped to clean the site with medications.
Then I treated the patient for tumors, and it may be that this artery has many branches, and it is not surprising if it appears in the joint of the leg or in the leg itself, causing him many pains and aching, as we mentioned in the section on anatomy and what we have presented.
Chapter 89.
On the incision on the generated lumps under the rib, and it is called the ulcer of the cattle disease.
This disease is called in some countries among us the ulcer of the cattle disease, because it often affects cattle and it is a small, single, generated lump that forms between the skin and the flesh and spreads throughout the body, causing swelling and connection.
It progresses gradually from one member to another until it perforates, where it has not perforated the skin at that site, and comes out and forms a ulceration from some of the corrupt humors, as it appears in the lumps and tumors, and loves to settle in the abdominal cavity.
And indeed, it is feared from its mischief that if it settles in the body and rises to the head and reaches the eye, perhaps it will open up there and come out, thus damaging the eye. This appears often. Therefore, if you want to treat it and extract it, then it must be done when it first appears and begins to progress gradually.
It is necessary to dissect above and below it with a strong ligature, then make an incision over it and extract it. If it has penetrated into the flesh and you do not find it, then apply a hot iron to the site until it is perforated, and beware of its damage to the eye, as we have said.
If you find it has settled in the head near the eyes, then press under it on the forehead strongly and steadily, then make an incision over it and extract it. And it is necessary to take care of the patient's body with sweet medications for the foul ulcers and to guard against the putrid matter that causes the inflammation.
Chapter 83.
On the incision for the disease that is recognized by the swelling.
This disease, which is called in our country "al-Nafar", is a abscess that appears on some of the limbs and then transfers from one limb to another, and I have seen it as I described to you.
I was called to a woman who had some numbness in her limbs, so I examined her arm and found a small swelling in the artery of the arm, and when it remained for an hour, I saw that swelling move with the pulse as the finger moves when it is inserted into the hollow.
If it moves from one place to another, the pain leaves that place and settles in the shoulder, then it remains for an hour until it spreads to the rest of the body, until it becomes in the other arm, and then I knew that it affects her entire body, as I observed.
I was amazed at the speed with which it transferred from one limb to another, and I had not seen this disease before with such a symptom, except that I had seen a group of people who experienced pain transferring from one limb to another, but I did not see it as clearly as I saw it in this woman.
And I did not think that it was because the woman was from the people of the desert, with a dry and rough skin, and uncovered arteries, so it was clear to me that this transferring sensation appeared because of this, and it is unlikely to appear in the people of the cities and villages, who have soft and hidden arteries.
If you want to treat it and its owner feels a sensation of discomfort, then the patient will become aware of it as we have mentioned, so press on it firmly with your fingers and hold it tightly until that constricted air is released and the spot becomes relaxed.
If you did not see it with your own eyes, treat it by massaging the affected limb and what is hidden of the air, and evacuate it like evacuating a stubborn abscess and a bruise, and treat it with medicaments.
Chapter 84.
On Removing Arrowheads.
Arrowheads may differ according to their types and according to the locations in which they are found in the body, and as for their difference according to their types, there are large and small ones, and some have triangular and quadrangular points.
And some have barbs and some have fragments, and as for those that are according to the members in which they are found, they are on different patterns, either the members are main vital organs such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, and stomach, and so on. So when an arrowhead falls in one of these organs and death symptoms appear, which I will describe to you later, it is necessary to hasten the removal of that arrowhead from them, for death often follows its owner in most cases. And when these bad symptoms do not appear to you, and the arrowhead is not lodged in the depth of the organ, then extract it and treat the wound. And among the signs of a head injury, if an arrowhead strikes the brain and penetrates the bone, and wounds the dura mater that covers the brain, then it produces severe headache, vertigo, and stupor.
And when these bad symptoms do not appear to you, and the arrowhead is not lodged in the depth of the organ, then extract it and treat the wound. And among the signs of a head injury, if an arrowhead strikes the brain and penetrates the bone, and wounds the dura mater that covers the brain, then it produces severe headache, vertigo, and stupor. And there is a redness in the eyes and a redness of the tongue, and convulsions, and confusion of mind, and a reversal of senses, and sometimes blood comes out from the nostrils or ears, and sometimes speech is cut off and the voice goes away, and a white frothy discharge emerges from the site of the wound, resembling pus, and it is drawn out like the liquid of meat.
If these signs appear to you, refrain from treating the limpness and extracting the arrowhead if it has not come out, and as for the signs of the arrowhead, if it has reached the heart and was close to the left nipple and felt as if it had been implanted in a solid body and not in an empty one.
Perhaps the arrowhead was moving with a motion similar to that of a pulse, and blood would flow out from the wound, which would be followed by numbness in the extremities and a cold sweat, and you should know that death is imminent without any doubt. And a sign of the arrowhead is if the lung is wounded, with a flow of frothy blood from the wound.
And the vessels that are below the neck become swollen and change the color of the limb, and they puff up with a faint puffing, and ask for inhalation of cold air; if the arrowhead has reached the diaphragm that is in the chest, then it is close to the small ribs and the puffing becomes severe with severe pain.
And all the organs of the shoulders sink, and if the arrowhead has reached the liver, it is followed by severe pain and a discharge from the wound of blood resembling the liver in its redness; and if the arrowhead has reached the stomach, perhaps something unripe from the food would be vomited out from the wound.
And the matter is clear, and if the arrowhead has reached the abdomen and become fixed in it, and something from the feces or urine or pus has come out from the wound, then there is no hope in treating it nor in extracting the arrowhead; for if the arrowhead has reached the bladder and urine has come out.
And something bursts out from it to the outside, and the pain intensifies on the limb, so you should know that it is dying; and as for the rest of the organs, such as the face, eye, throat, shoulder, arm, back, hip, leg, and similar ones, they have given up on the severe matter.
When the arrow did not meet with a sharp or blunt instrument, and it was not poisoned, I will tell you about some of what I have seen regarding these arrows to guide you in your treatment, which is that an arrow had lodged in a man's eye socket at the base of his nose.
I extracted it for him from the other side beneath the eyebrow and he was healed, and no harm occurred to his eye. I also extracted another arrow that had lodged in his eye beneath the lower eyelid, which had become embedded and only its small tip remained attached to the skin.
It was a large arrow from the arrows of the Qasi tribe, with a rhomboid iron head and no barb, so it healed quickly without any bad incident occurring to his eye. I also extracted another arrow from a Christian's throat, and the arrow was Arab-made.
He was the one with barbs, so I split it open between the ribs and it had lodged in his throat, so I manipulated it until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed. I also extracted another arrow from a man who had been struck in his belly, and we thought he would die from it.
He did not remain for a period of thirty days or thereabouts, and nothing changed in his condition. I split open on the arrow, manipulated it, and extracted it, and he was healed without any bad incident occurring to him. I also saw a man who had been struck by an arrow in his back, so I treated the wound and dressed it.
He did not remain for seven years, until the arrow came out from the bottom of his thigh. I also saw a woman who had been struck by an arrow in her belly, and I treated the wound, but the arrow remained without changing anything in her condition, and she did not find any harm in any of her natural functions.
I also saw another man who had been struck by an arrow in his face, and I treated the wound, but he did not find much pain. And there were many cases like this, and I extracted an arrow from a man of the Sultan's guard who had been struck in the middle of his nose, which had deviated slightly towards the right nostril.

Chapter 85.
On the sectioning of veins.
The veins that it is customary to section in the body are thirty, of which six are in the head: the two nabid veins behind the ears, known as the sensual; the two jugular veins in the neck, visible and apparent; and the two veins in the corners of the eyes, known as the inspecting.
And the vein that is in the middle of the forehead, and the vein that is at the side of the nose, and the two jugular veins in the neck, and the two veins on the upper lip from the mouth, and the two veins on the lower lip, and these are the known veins of the gullet, and the two veins under the tongue.
And as for the veins that are sectioned in the arm and hand, there are five: one is the cephalic, which is on the lateral side, and it is called the common vein of the head; and the median, which is the middle vein, composed of branches from the basilic and the cephalic, and it is commonly called the vein of the body.
The basilic vein, which is the topic in the inner aspect and is also called the umbilical vein, and the common people call it the "vein of the flank" and it is the one that lies on the thigh and it is the one that appears above the pubes, clearly visible.
And it is the vein between the speronal and condyloid, having two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one beneath the knee joint on the outer aspect, the second is the Safeen, located at the ankle on the inner aspect, and the vein of the ankle, located at the heel on the outer aspect.
And in the other leg, there are three veins like them; but as for the two veins behind the ears, they are of benefit in treating chronic and hectic diseases, and the affliction of the head and its chronic pains, and how they are beneficial in treating what I have described.
